PREFACE
         This code of the city of Grangeville, as supplemented, contains
ordinances up to and including ordinance 978, passed November 18, 2024.
Ordinances of the city adopted after said ordinance supersede the provisions of
this code to the extent that they are in conflict or inconsistent therewith.
Consult the city office in order to ascertain whether any particular provision
of the code has been amended, superseded or repealed.
                     American Legal Publishing
                     Cincinnati, Ohio
ORDINANCES PENDING REVIEW FOR CODIFICATION
Listed ordinances have been passed, but they are pending review by the
publisher, and they may not amend the code of ordinances. Additionally,
ordinances listed in this section may not show the original ordinances in their
entirety. Please contact the office of the clerk if there are any questions
concerning any listed ordinances.
ORDINANCE NO. 979
 
AN ORDINANCE OF THE CITY OF GRANGEVILLE, IDAHO, AMENDING TITLE 10, CHAPTER 10,
SUBSECTION 3A2 OF THE GRANGEVILLE CITY CODE RELATING TO NOTICE REQUIREMENTS FOR
VARIANCE APPLICATIONS; PROVIDING FOR SEVERABILITY; AND PROVIDING FOR AN
EFFECTIVE DATE.
 
WHEREAS, the City of Grangeville has determined that it is in the best interest
of its citizens to amend the notice requirements for variance applications to
streamline the process and reduce costs; and
 
WHEREAS, the City of Grangeville finds that providing notice by first class
mail is sufficient to ensure adequate notification to property owners within
three hundred feet (300') of a proposed variance area; and
 
WHEREAS, the City of Grangeville desires to amend Section 10-10-3A2 of the
Grangeville Municipal Code to reflect this change.
 
NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT ORDAINED BY THE MAYOR AND CITY COUNCIL OF THE CITY OF
GRANGEVILLE, IDAHO:
 
Section 1: Section 10-1-3A2 of the Grangeville Municipal Code is hereby amended
to read as follows:
 
2. With any application for a variance, the applicant shall, at the time the
application is filed with the City, provide the City Clerk with the names and
addresses of all persons owning any real property within three hundred feet
(300') of any portion of the area for which the variance is sought. Thereafter,
the City shall deliver to those persons owning property within three hundred
feet (300') shall be delivered either personally, or by certified first class
mail, a notice of a hearing that this section requires with the mailing and
notice having occurred at least fifteen (15) days prior to the time of such
hearing. In any notice of hearing there shall be language therein that includes
the content of subsection A3 of this section, describing the City's protest
procedure, in the event of objection."
 
   Section 2:   All ordinances or parts of ordinances in conflict herewith are
hereby repealed.
 
   Section 3: This ordinance shall become effective upon its passage, approval,
and publication in the Idaho County Free Press.
 
This ordinance passed under a suspension of the rule requiring three readings
on separate days at a regular meeting of the City Council held on the 17 th day
of March, 2025.
 
                  __________________________________________
                  WES LESTER, Mayor

TONYA KENNEDY, City Clerk
ORDINANCE NO. 982
AN ORDINANCE OF THE CITY OF GRANGEVILLE, IDAHO COUNTY, STATE OF IDAHO, ADDING
CHAPTER 7 OF TITLE 6 TO THE GRANGEVILLE MUNICIPAL CODE PERTAINING TO CAMPING ON
PUBLIC PROPERTY; PROVIDING A STATEMENT OF FINDINGS AND AUTHORITY; PROVIDING
THAT UNLESS OTHERWISE PROVIDED UNDER SAID CHAPTER 7 OR AUTHORIZED THE CITY OR
BY LAW, IT SHALL BE UNLAWFUL TO CAMP ON PUBLIC PROPERTY; PROVIDING FOR
PENALTIES FOR VIOLATIONS OF SAID CHAPTER 7; PROVIDING THAT ANY PERSON VIOLATING
SAID CHAPTER 7 SHALL BE GUILTY OF A MISDEMEANOR; PROVIDING THAT VIOLATIONS OF
SAID CHAPTER 7 SHALL BE PUNISHED BY A FINE AS ESTABLISHED IN THE CITY OF
GRANGEVILLE MASTER FEE SCHEDULE OR 6 MONTHS IN THE COUNTY JAIL, OR BOTH;
DECLARING THAT VIOLATION OF SAID CHAPTER 7 OF TITLE 6 SHALL CONSTITUTE A PUBLIC
NUISANCE; PROVIDING THAT SAID CHAPTER 7 OF TITLE 6 DOES NOT SUPERSEDE OR REVOKE
ANY OTHER APPLICABLE LAWS, REGULATIONS, CODES OR ORDINANCES PERTAINING TO
CAMPING ON PUBLIC PROPERTY EXCEPT AS PROVIDED IN THIS ORDINANCE; PROVIDING FOR
DESIGNATION OF SPECIAL CAMPING ZONES; PROVIDING THAT IT IS UNLAWFUL FOR ANY
PERSON TO KNOWINGLY REFUSE OR FAIL TO VACATE OR CEASE CAMPING WITH A SPECIAL
CAMPING ZONE UPON EXPIRATION OR TERMINATION OF THE SPECIAL CAMPING ZONE
DESIGNATION, OR TO VIOLATE ANY TERM OR CONDITION OF A SPECIAL CAMPING ZONE
DESIGNATION; PROVIDING DEFINITIONS; PROVIDING FOR SEVERABILITY; PROVIDING FOR
REPEAL OF CONFLICTING ORDINANCES; PROVIDING THAT THIS ORDINANCE SHALL BE
EFFECTIVE UPON ADOPTION AND PUBLICATION AS PROVIDED BY LAW.
 
BE IT ORDAINED by the Mayor and Council of the City of Grangeville as follows:
 
SECTION 1:   Grangeville Municipal Code § 6-7 shall be added as follows
 
6-7-1: TITLE:
 
This Chapter shall be known and may be cited as the City of Grangeville Camping
Ordinance.
 
6-7-2: DEFINITIONS:
 
The definitions set forth in this Chapter shall govern the construction of this
Chapter, unless the context otherwise requires. As used in this chapter, the
following terms shall have the following meanings:
 
CAMP and CAMPING: “Camp” and “camping” shall mean the use or occupancy of any
public property as a temporary or permanent place of residence, lodging,
dwelling, habitation or abode, whether or not such conduct occurs within or
outside of any temporary or permanent structure, shelter, other enclosure or
vehicle of any kind or nature. Prima facie evidence of camping may include, but
is not limited to, storage of personal belongings, using tents or other
temporary structures, shelters or enclosures for sleeping or storage of
personal belongings, carrying on cooking activities or making any fire in an
unauthorized area, or any of these activities in combination with one another
or in combination with either sleeping or making preparations to sleep
(including the laying down of bedding for the purpose of sleeping).
 
CITY PROPERTY: “City property” shall mean 1) any and all real property owned by
the city, whether inside or outside of city limits, including but not limited
to any city park, playground, ball field, sports field, recreational field, ski
hill, or parking lot, and 2) any and all city streets, sidewalks, alleys and
rights of way within the city.
 
PUBLIC PROPERTY: “Public property” shall mean 1) any and all city property, and
2) any and all public streets, sidewalks, alleys and rights of way within the
city.
 
6-7-3   CAMPING ON PUBLIC PROPERTY PROHIBITED:
 
Unless otherwise provided under this chapter or authorized by the city or by
law, it is unlawful for any person to camp upon or within any public property
or any portion thereof.
 
6-7-4   SPECIAL CAMPING ZONES AND CAMPING ON LEASED CITY PROPERTY:
 
The city council may by resolution designate any portion of any city property
as a "special camping zone" authorizing temporary camping upon or within said
city property for events or activities such as sporting or school events, on
such terms and conditions as the city council deems in the best interest of the
city. Such a resolution shall describe the portion of city property included in
the special camping zone and specify the inclusive dates and times during which
camping within the zone are permitted. Any such designated camping zones shall
be marked with signage identifying the city property included in the zone and
the inclusive dates and times during which camping within the zone is
permitted. It shall be unlawful for any person camping within any designated
special camping zone to knowingly a) violate any term or condition of the
special camping zone designation established by the city council, or b) refuse
or otherwise fail to vacate and cease camping within said any designated
special camping zone upon expiration or earlier termination of the special
camping zone designation. The city council may by resolution from time to time
amend or terminate any special camping zone designation made by the city
council under this section as the city council deems it in the best interest of
the city. Any camping on city property leased to a third party shall be at the
discretion and control of the third party, subject to the terms of the lease
and any applicable laws.
 
6-7-5   VIOLATIONS – PUBLIC NUISANCE- OTHER CITY REMEDIES PRESERVED:
 
A.   Every person who pleads guilty to or is found guilty of violating any
provision of this chapter is guilty of a misdemeanor.
 
B.   Any violation of this chapter shall be punishable by incarceration in the
county jail up to 6 months, or a fine as established in the master fee
schedule, or both said jail and fine.
 
C.   Any violation of this chapter is hereby also declared to be a public
nuisance. The city may also pursue all other and further remedies provided by
this code or otherwise provided by law against any person who has violated or
is violating any provision of this chapter, including but not limited to as
provided under trespass laws and nuisance laws, with all remedies of city being
cumulative and non-exclusive.
 
 
6-7-6   ADDITIONAL PROVISIONS:
 
This chapter supplements and does not supersede nor revoke in whole or in part
any other applicable federal, state, county or city laws, regulations, codes or
ordinances regulating, prohibiting, or restricting camping, sleeping, dwelling
or parking upon any public street, sidewalk, alley, right of way or any other
public property.
 
 
SECTION 2:   This ordinance is severable. In the event any portion of this
ordinance is deemed unenforceable by a court of competent jurisdiction, the
remaining portions of this ordinance not so affected shall remain in effect.
 
SECTION 3:   All ordinances or parts of ordinances in conflict herewith are
hereby repealed.
 
SECTION 4: This ordinance shall become effective upon its passage, approval,
and publication by summary in the Idaho County Free Press.
 
This ordinance passed under a suspension of the rule requiring three readings
on separate days at a regular meeting of the City Council held on the 7 th day
of July, 2025.
 
DULY APPROVED AND ADOPTED by the Mayor and City Council of the City of
Grangeville this 7 th day of July, 2025.
 
                  CITY OF GRANGEVILLE
 
                  By: _______________________________
                     WES LESTER, Mayor

TONYA KENNEDY, City Clerk
ORDINANCE NO. 983
AN ORDINANCE OF THE CITY OF GRANGEVILLE, IDAHO, ADDING SECTION 6 TO CHAPTER 2
TO TITLE 3 OF THE GRANGEVILLE MUNICIPAL CODE, PROVIDING FOR THE RECOVERY OF
COSTS ASSOCIATED WITH FIRE SUPPRESSION AND PROTECTION SERVICES; ESTABLISHING
PROCEDURES FOR BILLING AND COLLECTION; PROVIDING FOR SEVERABILITY; PROVIDING
FOR REPEAL OF CONFLICTING ORDINANCES; AND PROVIDING AN EFFECTIVE DATE.
BE IT ORDAINED BY THE MAYOR AND CITY COUNCIL OF THE CITY OF GRANGEVILLE, IDAHO:
SECTION 1. Purpose and Intent.
The purpose of this ordinance is to establish the authority for the City of
Grangeville to recover the actual costs incurred by the City in providing fire
suppression and protection services in response to personal property fires
within the City limits, and to recover costs associated with responding to
false alarms. The intent of this ordinance is to promote public safety, reduce
the number of false alarms, and ensure that those who benefit from or
necessitate fire department services bear an appropriate portion of the costs
of providing such services.
SECTION 2. Definitions.
For the purposes of this Chapter, the following terms shall have the meanings
set forth below:
A. "Actual Costs" means all costs, direct and indirect, incurred by the City of
Grangeville in response to a personal property fire or false alarm. These costs
include, but are not limited to: personnel costs (including overtime),
operational costs, costs for the use of materials, equipment costs (including
damage, repair, and replacement), administrative costs, and other reasonable
expenses attributable to the fire response or false alarm response.
B. "False Alarm" means the activation of a fire alarm system resulting in the
response of the Fire Department when no actual fire or emergency exists. This
includes activation caused by mechanical failure, malfunction, improper
installation, lack of proper maintenance, negligent activation by the owner or
occupant, or any other activation not caused by a fire or other emergency
requiring response by the Fire Department.
C. "Fire Department" means the Grangeville Volunteer Fire Department or any
other fire department providing services on behalf of the City of Grangeville.
D. "Fire Chief" means the Fire Chief of the City of Grangeville or their
designee.
E. "Owner" means any person, agent, firm, corporation, or entity having a legal
or equitable interest in personal property on which fire suppression services
were provided or to which the Fire Department responded due to a false alarm.
F. "Personal Property" means any movable or intangible property that is subject
to ownership, including but not limited to vehicles, equipment, and other
similar items.
SECTION 3. Authority to Recover Costs.
A. The City of Grangeville shall have the authority to charge and recover from
the owner of any personal property the actual costs incurred by the City for
providing fire suppression and protection services in response to a fire on
such personal property.
B. The City shall have the authority to charge and recover from the owner of
any property the actual costs incurred by the City for responding to false
alarms originating from such property, subject to the limitations set forth in
Section 3(D) of this ordinance.
C. This authority applies regardless of whether the owner of the personal
property requested such services.
D. For false alarms, the following schedule of charges shall apply:
1.   First through fourth false alarm within a calendar year: Written warning,
no charge.
2.   Fifth and subsequent false alarms within a calendar year: Actual costs
incurred, plus an administrative fee as established in the master fee schedule.
E. The City's authority to recover costs under this ordinance is in addition to
any other remedies available to the City under state and local law.
SECTION 4. Determination of Costs.
A. The Fire Chief shall be responsible for determining the actual costs
incurred in responding to a personal property fire.
B. The determination shall be based on actual expenses incurred, including but
not limited to:
1.   Personnel costs, including regular and overtime wages, benefits, and
workers' compensation;
2.   Equipment costs, based on hourly rates established by the City or FEMA
Schedule of Equipment Rates, whichever is greater;
3.   Cost of materials and supplies used, damaged, or destroyed;
4.   Administrative costs associated with the incident and cost recovery;
5.   Any specialized services required, including but not limited to hazardous
materials response, technical rescue, or mutual aid; and
6.   Any other reasonable costs attributable to the fire response.
C. The Fire Chief shall maintain detailed records of all costs associated with
each fire response.
SECTION 5. Billing Procedures.
A. Within sixty (60) days after the conclusion of a personal property fire
incident, the City shall send an itemized bill to the owner of the personal
property, detailing the actual costs incurred for fire suppression services.
B. The bill shall include:
1.   The date, time, and location of the personal property fire;
2.   A detailed itemization of all costs being charged;
3.   The total amount due;
4.   Payment terms and due date;
5.   Information regarding the process for appealing the bill; and
6.   Contact information for questions regarding the bill.
C. Payment shall be due within thirty (30) days from the date of the invoice.
SECTION 6. Appeals Process.
A. Any personal property owner who wishes to contest a bill for actual costs
may file a written appeal with the City Clerk within fifteen (15) days of
receiving the bill.
B. The appeal shall state the specific grounds upon which the bill is contested
and include any supporting documentation.
C. The City Council shall consider the appeal at a regular meeting within
forty-five (45) days of receipt of the appeal. The property owner shall be
notified of the date, time, and location of the meeting at which the appeal
will be considered.
D. The City Council's decision on the appeal shall be final.
SECTION 7. Collection of Unpaid Bills.
A. If a personal property owner fails to pay the bill for actual costs within
thirty (30) days of the due date, and has not filed an appeal, the bill shall
be considered delinquent.
B. The City may pursue any and all legal remedies to collect delinquent bills,
including but not limited to:
1.   Referral to a collection agency;
2.   Filing a civil action in a court of competent jurisdiction;
C. In addition to the actual costs, the property owner shall be responsible for
any interest, penalties, and collection costs associated with a delinquent
bill.
SECTION 8. Exemptions.
A. The following are exempt from the provisions of this ordinance relating to
personal property fire suppression cost recovery:
1.   Fires caused by natural disasters such as lightning strikes, earthquakes,
or other acts of God, unless exacerbated by the negligence of the property
owner;
2.   Fires occurring on personal property owned by the City of Grangeville; and
3.   Fires that spread to a property through no fault of the property owner.
B. The following are exempt from the provisions of this ordinance relating to
false alarm cost recovery:
1.   False alarms that occur during electrical storms, earthquakes, or other
severe weather conditions;
2.   False alarms that are activated during testing of the alarm system,
provided that the Fire Department has been notified in advance;
3.   False alarms that occur within 30 days after installation of a new alarm
system; and
4.   False alarms that occur on property owned by the City of Grangeville.
C. The Fire Chief shall make the initial determination regarding whether an
exemption applies. This determination may be appealed through the process
outlined in Section 6.
SECTION 9. Use of Recovered Funds.
All funds recovered under this ordinance shall be deposited into the general
fund.
SECTION 10. Annual Review.
The City Council shall review this ordinance and the fee structure annually to
ensure that the fees charged reflect the actual costs incurred by the City for
providing fire suppression services.
SECTION 11. Severability.
If any section, subsection, sentence, clause, phrase, or portion of this
ordinance is for any reason held invalid or unconstitutional by any court of
competent jurisdiction, such portion shall be deemed a separate, distinct, and
independent provision and such holding shall not affect the validity of the
remaining portions of this ordinance.
SECTION 12. Repeal of Conflicting Ordinances.
All ordinances or parts of ordinances in conflict herewith are hereby repealed.
SECTION 13: This ordinance shall become effective upon its passage, approval,
and publication in the Idaho County Free Press.
This ordinance passed under a suspension of the rule requiring three readings
on separate days held at a regular meeting of the City Council on the 7 th day
of July, 2025.
   
                  __________________________________________
                  WES LESTER, Mayor
 
ATTEST:
 
 
___________________________________
TONYA KENNEDY, City Clerk
 
                           (Seal)
 
ADOPTING ORDINANCE
AN ORDINANCE
AN ORDINANCE FOR REVISING, COMPILING AND CODIFYING THE GENERAL ORDINANCES OF
THE CITY OF GRANGEVILLE, IDAHO.
BE IT ORDAINED BY THE MAYOR AND CITY COUNCIL OF THE CITY OF GRANGEVILLE, IDAHO
COUNTY, IDAHO;
Section 1. All ordinances of a general nature now in force in the City of
Grangeville, Idaho County, Idaho, as revised, compiled and codified and
hereafter set forth are hereby adopted, passed, published and declared to
constitute the official Code of the City of Grangeville according to Chapter 5,
Title 50, Idaho Code, as amended.
Section 2. This ordinance and all ordinances of a general nature contained in
this Code shall be in full force and effect upon its passage and upon
publication in the official newspaper.
This ordinance passed under suspension of rules, upon which a roll call vote
was duly taken, is hereby enacted at a meeting of the City Council held
February 2, 1959 at 7:30 P.M.
Approved by the Mayor and City Council this second day of February, 1959.

TITLE 1
ADMINISTRATION
CHAPTER 1
OFFICIAL CITY CODE
SECTION:
1-1-1: Municipal Code Of The City Of Grangeville
1-1-2: Effect Of Repealing Ordinances
1-1-3: Rules For Construction
1-1-4: Definitions
1-1-1: MUNICIPAL CODE OF THE CITY OF GRANGEVILLE:
This compilation, revision and codification of the general ordinances of the
City of Grangeville is hereby declared to be and shall hereafter constitute the
official code of general ordinances of the City of Grangeville.
Said Code shall hereafter be known and cited as the GRANGEVILLE CITY CODE, and
a copy or copies of such Code in printed form shall be received, without
further proof, as the ordinances of permanent and general effect of the City of
Grangeville, in all courts and administrative tribunals of this State.
Any ordinance amending this Code shall set forth in full the section or
sections of the Code being amended, and this shall constitute a sufficient
compliance with any statutory requirement that no ordinance or any section
thereof shall be revised or amended unless the new ordinance sets forth the
revised ordinance or amended section in full. (1959 Code)
1-1-2: EFFECT OF REPEALING ORDINANCES:
The repeal of ordinances as provided shall not affect any right which has
accrued, any duty imposed, any penalty incurred, nor any action or proceedings
as commenced under or by virtue of the ordinances repealed, nor the tenure of
office of any person holding office at the time when such ordinances take
effect; nor shall the repeal of any ordinance thereby have the effect of
reviving any ordinance therefor repealed or superseded. (1959 Code)
1-1-3: RULES FOR CONSTRUCTION:
In the construction of the official Code and all ordinances amendatory thereof
or supplementary thereto the following rules shall be observed unless such
construction would be inconsistent with the manifest intent of the legislative
body or repugnant to the context.
   A.   Intent To Defraud: Whenever, by any of the provisions of the official
Code, an intent to defraud is required in order to constitute an offense, it is
sufficient if an intent appears to defraud any person, association or body
politic or any combination of persons.
   B.   Liability Of Employers And Agents: When the provision herein contained
prohibits the commission or omission of an act, not only the person actually
doing the prohibited thing or omitting the directed act, but also the employer
and all other persons concerned or aiding or abetting the person shall be
guilty of the offense described and liable to the penalty set forth.
   C.   Title Of Sections And Subsections: The title of any section or
subsection of this official Code shall be deemed in nowise to restrict, qualify
or to limit the effect of the provisions set forth and contained in such
section or subsection.
   D.   Constitutionality; Effect Of: Should any portion of this official Code
be declared by any court of competent jurisdiction to be unconstitutional or
void, such adjudication shall in no way affect the remaining portion of this
Code. (1959 Code)
1-1-4: DEFINITIONS:
The singular number includes the plural; words used in the present include the
future; words used in the masculine gender comprehend as well, the feminine and
neuter.
DAY, MONTH, QUARTER, YEAR: "Day" means any twenty four (24) hour period from
midnight to midnight; "month" means a calendar month unless otherwise
expressed; "quarter" means any three (3) month period, ending with the last day
of March, June, September and December; and "year" means any one calendar year
unless otherwise expressed.
KNOWINGLY: Imports only a knowledge that the facts exist which brings the act
or omission within the provisions of these chapters. It does not require any
knowledge of the unlawfulness of such act or omission.
LAND, REAL ESTATE AND REAL PROPERTY: Includes lands, tenements, hereditaments,
water rights, possessory rights and claims.
NEGLECT, NEGLIGENCE, NEGLIGENT AND NEGLIGENTLY: Imports a want of such
attention to the nature or probable consequences of the act or omission as a
prudent man ordinarily bestows in acting in his own concern.
OATH: Includes "affirmation" and the word "swear" includes the word "affirm".
Every mode of oral statement under oath or affirmation is embraced in the term
"testify" and every written one in the term "depose".
OFFICER: Includes officers and boards in charge of departments and the members
of such boards and such reference as use of the word "Municipality" shall mean
this City. "Clerk" or "Treasurer" and others shall mean the City Clerk or City
Treasurer as the case may be applicable.
OFFICIAL TIME: Whenever used for the conduct of municipal affairs within the
City of Grangeville, Idaho County, Idaho, shall be Pacific Daylight Saving
Time, from the last Sunday in April of each year to the last Sunday in October
and all municipal affairs shall be conducted according to said standard of
time.
OWNER: Applied to a building or land, shall include any part owner, joint
owner, tenant in common, joint tenant or lessee of the whole or of a part of
such building or land.
PERSON: Includes bodies politic and corporate, partnerships, associations and
corporations.
PERSONAL PROPERTY: Includes every description of money, goods, chattels,
effects, evidence of rights in action, and all written instruments by which any
pecuniary obligation, right or title to property is created, acknowledged,
transferred, increased, defeated, discharged or diminished, and every right or
interest therein.
PROPERTY: Includes both real and personal property.
PUBLIC THOROUGHFARE: Includes streets, alleys, lanes, courts, boulevards,
public ways, public squares, public places and sidewalks.
SHALL/MAY: Shall is mandatory, may is discretionary.
SIGNATURE: Includes any name, mark or sign written with the intent to
authenticate any instrument of writing.
TENANT, OCCUPANT: Applied to a building or land, shall include any person who
occupies the whole or any part of such building or land whether alone or with
others.
WILFULLY: When applied to the intent with which an act is done or omitted,
implies simply a purpose or willingness to commit the act or make the omission
referred to. It does not require any intent to violate law or to injure another
or to acquire an advantage.
WRITING: Includes printing, writing and typewriting.
Words prohibiting anything being done, except in accordance with a license or
permit or authority from a board or officers, shall be construed as giving such
board or officer power to license or permit or authorize such thing to be done.
Whenever in this Code it is provided that anything must be done, to the
approval of or subject to the direction of the enforcing officer, this shall be
construed to give such officer only the power to determine whether the rules
and regulations established in this Code have been complied with and shall not
be construed as giving such officer discretionary powers. (Revised Code 1959;
amd. Ord. 358, 4-1-1963)
CHAPTER 2
CITY LIMITS
SECTION:
1-2-1: City Limits Designated
1-2-1: CITY LIMITS DESIGNATED:

CHAPTER 3
MUNICIPAL AFFAIRS
SECTION:
1-3-1: Corporate Seal
1-3-2: Municipal Depositories
1-3-3: Official Newspaper
1-3-4: City Elections; Voting Hours
1-3-1: CORPORATE SEAL:
   A.   Design: The Corporate Seal of the City of Grangeville shall be circular
in form with inner and outer circles. The outer circle shall be two inches (2")
in diameter, and the inner circle one and one-fourth inches (11/4") in
diameter. It shall bear upon the space between the two (2) circles the words,
"Grangeville, Idaho, Idaho County", and upon the space within the inner circle
the words, "Incorporated October, 1897", and the word "SEAL", as follows:
[https://export.amlegal.com/media/b15888aa0cf0ae458f20080f502f937b1536fcd0/
IMAGES/0-0-0-1198.gif]
   B.   Adoption: The Seal described in the above Section of this Chapter be
and the same is hereby adopted as the Corporate Seal of the City of
Grangeville, Idaho. (1959 Code)
1-3-2: MUNICIPAL DEPOSITORIES:
   A.   Designated: The Bank of Central Idaho, Grangeville, Idaho, and the
First Security Bank of Idaho, Grangeville Branch, N.A., Grangeville, Idaho, are
hereby designated as the official depositories for Municipal funds. (Ord. 324,
6-11-1959)
   B.   Demand Funds: Pursuant to Idaho Code 50-1013, the City Clerk/Treasurer
be and is hereby authorized to deposit all demand funds of the City in such
qualified depository or depositories as defined by Idaho Code title 57, chapter
1, as shall be determined by the City Council by competitive bidding or other
means generally accepted as a standard business practice, all as authorized by
Idaho Code 57-128.
Prior to and until a depository or depositories shall be designated by the City
Council, pursuant to Idaho Code 57-128, the City Clerk/Treasurer be and is
hereby authorized to continue the existing practice of keeping City money
deposited with each designated depository within the City or within Idaho
County in such proportion of the total deposits of the City as capital and the
surplus of each depository bears to the total capital and surplus of all
designated depositories within the City or Idaho County. (Ord. 564, 7-7-1983)
1-3-3: OFFICIAL NEWSPAPER:
The Idaho County Free Press, Grangeville, Idaho, is hereby designated as the
official newspaper. (1959 Code)
1-3-4: CITY ELECTIONS; VOTING HOURS:
Pursuant to the provisions of Idaho Code 50-453 as amended, the polls at all
general and special City elections shall be opened at twelve o'clock (12:00)
noon on election day and remain open until all registered voters of that
precinct have voted or until eight o'clock (8:00) P.M. of the same day,
whichever occurs first. (Ord. 703, 8-18-1997)
CHAPTER 4
GENERAL PENALTY
SECTION:
1-4-1: General Penalty
1-4-2: Default
1-4-3: Driving While Intoxicated
1-4-4: Labor
1-4-5: License
1-4-6: Application
1-4-1: GENERAL PENALTY:
Any person convicted of a violation of any section of this Code shall be fined
as established in the master fee schedule for any one offense, and such person
may be confined in the Municipal Jail for a period of not more than thirty (30)
days. Either or both such fine and imprisonment may be imposed. (Ord. 349, 12-
4-1961; amd. Ord. 925, 10-1-2018)
1-4-2: DEFAULT:
Any person in default of payment of any fine imposed shall be imprisoned in the
Municipal Jail for a period of one day for each five dollars ($5.00) of such
fine. (1959 Code)
1-4-3: DRIVING WHILE INTOXICATED:
Any person convicted of driving a motor vehicle while intoxicated or under the
influence of intoxicating liquor or narcotic drugs shall be fined in the amount
as established in the master fee schedule and may also be confined in the
Municipal Jail for not more than thirty (30) days; provided, that upon
conviction, said person shall also surrender his driver's license to the court.
(1959 Code; amd. Ord. 925, 10-1-2018)
1-4-4: LABOR:
Any person imprisoned under the provisions of this chapter may be put to work
for the benefit of the City for the term of his imprisonment. No female
prisoner shall be required to work in public, nor shall any prisoner be
required to work on Sunday. (1959 Code)
1-4-5: LICENSE:
When a person is convicted of a violation of any section of this Code, any
license previously issued to him by the City may be revoked by the court or by
the Municipal Governing Body. (1959 Code)
1-4-6: APPLICATION:
The penalty provided in this chapter shall be applicable to every section of
this Code the same as though it were part of each and every separate section.
Any person convicted of a violation of any section of this Code, where any duty
is prescribed or obligation imposed, or where any act which is of a continuing
nature is forbidden or declared to be unlawful, shall be deemed guilty of a
misdemeanor. A separate offense shall be deemed committed upon each day such
duty or obligation remains unperformed or such act continues, unless otherwise
specifically provided in this Code. (1959 Code)
CHAPTER 5
MAYOR
SECTION:
1-5-1: Duties
1-5-2: Contracts
1-5-3: Rewards
1-5-4: Pardons
1-5-5: Veto Power
1-5-6: Accounts Of Officers
1-5-7: Police Power
1-5-8: May Require Aid
1-5-9: Other Powers
1-5-1: DUTIES:
The Mayor, the superintending and administrative officer of the City, shall
devote so much of his time to the duties of his office as an efficient and
faithful discharge thereof may require. He shall preside at all meetings of the
City Council and shall have a vote when the City Council is equally divided,
and call special meetings of the City Council when necessary. He shall appoint
all officers and employees of the City, subject to the approval of the City
Council, and have such other powers as the City Council may prescribe. He shall
from time to time provide for the City Council such information and recommend
such measures as he may deem beneficial to the City. He shall examine the
grounds of all complaints against any officer of the City to determine
existence of a violation or neglect of duty and report to the City Council the
evidence thereof, if deemed sufficient for the removal of said officer. He
shall require that every officer, on the expiration of his term of office or
resignation or removal, deliver to his successor all assets belonging to such
office. He shall perform all other duties required and necessary for the
efficient operation of the business of the City. (1959 Code)
1-5-2: CONTRACTS:
The Mayor is authorized and empowered to sign his name officially for and in
behalf of the City on all contracts, documents and papers to which the City is
a party, and to require that the conditions in any instrument are faithfully
performed. He may borrow money on the credit of the City when so authorized by
the City Council. (1959 Code)
1-5-3: REWARDS:
The Mayor, whenever he deems it expedient, is hereby empowered to offer a
reward not exceeding one hundred dollars ($100.00) for the arrest and
conviction of any person charged with violating any of the provisions of this
Code. (1959 Code)
1-5-4: PARDONS:
The Mayor is empowered to grant a pardon to any person imprisoned for a
violation of any of the provisions of this Code, and to remit so much of any
fine or forfeiture as in his judgment he may deem just and reasonable, and he
shall report such remittance or pardon to the City Council at its next meeting.
(1959 Code)
1-5-5: VETO POWER:
The Mayor shall have power to veto or sign any ordinance passed by the City
Council, provided, that any ordinance vetoed by the Mayor may be passed over
his veto by a vote of two-thirds (2/3) of the members of the City Council, and
should the Mayor neglect or refuse to sign any ordinance, the same shall become
law without his signature after the next regular meeting of the City Council.
(1959 Code)
1-5-6: ACCOUNTS OF OFFICERS:
The Mayor shall have the power to require any officer of the City to exhibit
his accounts or other papers and to make reports to the City Council in writing
on any subject or matter pertaining to the office. (1959 Code)
1-5-7: POLICE POWER:
The Mayor shall have jurisdiction over all places within five (5) miles of the
corporate limits of the City for the enforcement of any health or quarantine
ordinance and regulation and shall have jurisdiction in all matters, excepting
taxation, within one-half (1/2) mile of the corporate limits of the City. (1959
Code)
1-5-8: MAY REQUIRE AID:
The Mayor is hereby authorized to call on every male inhabitant of the City
over the age of eighteen (18) and under the age of fifty (50) years to aid in
enforcing the law. (1959 Code)
1-5-9: OTHER POWERS:
The Mayor shall have all other powers provided by State statute or by specific
provisions of this Code. (1959 Code)
CHAPTER 6
CITY COUNCIL
SECTION:
1-6-1: Duties
1-6-2: Election Of Councilmen
1-6-3: Vacancy; How Filled
1-6-4: Time And Place Of Meetings
1-6-5: Elect President Of The Council
1-6-6: Consent Agenda
1-6-7: Conduct Of Officials
1-6-1: DUTIES:
Members of the City Council, the legislative and policy making branch of the
City, shall devote so much of their time to the duties of their office as an
efficient and faithful discharge thereof may require. They shall attend
meetings of the City Council unless lawfully excused therefrom by the Mayor or
by a majority of the remaining members, and perform all duties which by the
nature of their office they should reasonably perform, such as the passing of
ordinances, resolutions and the investigation and study of work done for the
City according to the committees upon which they may severally be appointed by
the Mayor. (1959 Code)
1-6-2: ELECTION OF COUNCILMEN:
Councilmen shall be henceforth nominated and elected at large from the City in
the manner prescribed by Idaho Code title 50, chapter 4. (Ord. 703, 8-18-1997)
1-6-3: VACANCY; HOW FILLED:
A vacancy on the City Council shall be filled by appointment by the Mayor with
the consent of the City Council, which appointee shall serve only until the
next general City election, at which election such vacancy shall be filled for
the balance of the original term. (Ord. 406, 10-13-1969)
1-6-4: TIME AND PLACE OF MEETINGS:
   A.   The City Council shall hold regular sessions in the Council Chambers on
the first and third Mondays of each month at six o'clock (6:00) P.M. (Ord. 932,
4-15-2019)
1-6-5: ELECT PRESIDENT OF THE COUNCIL:
At the time of taking office, the City Council shall elect one of its members
President of the City Council who shall preside at all meetings of the City
Council and perform all other duties of the Mayor in the absence of the Mayor;
and, in the absence of the President the City Council shall elect one of their
members to occupy his place temporarily, who shall be styled Acting President
of the City Council, and the President and Acting President, when occupying the
place of Mayor, shall have the same privileges as other members of the City
Council and all actions of the President and Acting President, while so acting,
shall be binding upon the City Council and upon the City as if performed by the
Mayor. (1959 Code; amd. Ord. 927, 10-15-2018)
1-6-6: CONSENT AGENDA:
   A.   When the City Clerk determines that an agenda item is of a routine and
noncontroversial nature, such City Clerk shall present such item of business at
a regular meeting of the City Council as part of the consent agenda.
   B.   Items of business which may be considered on the consent agenda may
include, but not be limited to, the following: approval of minutes; approval of
citizen appointments; referrals to committees; approval of reports; approval of
authorization of communications; approval of resolutions or other items which
had been considered by the City Council at earlier meetings; approval of new or
renewal requests for alcoholic beverage licenses; the setting of public
hearings.
   C.   The consent agenda may be considered by the City Council as a single
item and may be introduced by a motion to approve the consent agenda.
   D.   On objection to the inclusion of any item on the consent agenda by any
member of the City Council or by the Mayor, that item shall be forthwith
removed from the consent agenda and forthwith considered on the regular City
Council agenda in accordance with the other rules governing City meetings.
Neither a formal motion or a second is necessary to remove an item from the
consent agenda. Such objections shall be recorded prior to taking the vote to
approve the consent agenda items. Approval of the consent agenda items will not
affect the consideration of any item removed from the consent agenda.
   E.   There shall be no debate or discussion of any item on a consent agenda
beyond asking questions for a simple verification or classification.
   F.   Approval of the motion to approve the consent agenda shall be fully
equivalent to approval, adoption or enactment of each motion, resolution, or
other item of business thereon exactly as if each had been acted upon
individually. Approval of the motion must be by a roll call vote. The City
Clerk shall record in the City Council minutes each item passed under the
consent agenda, individually and in full. However, no item shall be placed on
the consent agenda which the law requires to be acted upon by ordinance. (Ord.
570, 2-21-1984; amd. Ord. 927, 10-15-2018)
1-6-7: CONDUCT OF OFFICIALS:
In order to ensure fair and equitable treatment by Council members and City
officials this section is adopted describing a general Code of Ethics and
civility to which each citizen is entitled.
   A.   Confidence and respect can be best promoted if every public official
and employee, whether paid or unpaid, and whether elected or appointed will
uniformly:
      1.   Treat all citizens with courtesy, impartiality, fairness and
equality under the law; and
      2.   Avoid both actual and potential conflicts between their private
self-interest and the public interest.
   B.   Helping public officials and employees achieve these goals is one of
the objectives of this section.
   C.   If a Council member discloses a conflict of interest under the Idaho
State Ethics in Government Act, and then refuses to abstain from voting or
otherwise attempts to take further actions on the matter in conflict, then the
City Council and all other individual Councilmen present with no conflict shall
vote on whether or not to allow the Council member with the conflict to act on
the matter in question. (Ord. 750, 9-23-2002; amd. Ord. 927, 10-15-2018)
CHAPTER 7
MUNICIPAL OFFICERS AND EMPLOYEES
(Rep. by Ord. 928, 12-17-2018)
CHAPTER 8
ELECTION PRECINCTS
