CHAPTER 9
INITIATIVE AND REFERENDUM
SECTION:
1-9-1: Procedure For Filing Petitions
1-9-1: PROCEDURE FOR FILING PETITIONS 1 :
   A.   There is hereby established a procedure for the filing of petitions for
direct legislation by the people through the means of initiative and referendum
in the City. A petition for initiative or referendum shall substantially comply
in form for requirements of signature, verification of valid petitions and
printing of petitions with Idaho Code 34-1701 through 34-1705, which sections,
where not in conflict herewith, are hereby adopted by this reference. The City
Clerk shall keep three (3) copies of such sections on file in her office in the
City Hall, Grangeville, Idaho.
In addition, to the requirements of forms set out above, before any initiative
or referendum shall be placed upon any election ballot, there shall be affixed
thereto the signatures of petitioners equal in number to twenty percent (20%)
of the total number of voters registered to vote at the last general election
in the City.
   B.   No petition for referendum may be filed unless more than sixty (60)
days has expired following the final adoption of the City ordinance to be
subject to such referendum.
   C.   In the event that there is no general or primary election scheduled
within ninety (90) days of the final certification of the petition for
initiative or referendum, then not more than ninety (90) days following such
certification, a special election on such initiative or referendum shall be
provided for. However, in the event that a primary or general election will
follow within ninety (90) days of the final certification of the petition, then
such initiative or referendum will be submitted at the time of the said general
or primary election.
   D.   As part of the petition for referendum, it shall be necessary to
include the entire text of the ordinance or legislation sought to be repealed.
Likewise, as part of any initiative, it shall be necessary that the entire text
of the proposed ordinance or legislation be a part of the petition for
initiative.
   E.   Notwithstanding the other provisions of Idaho Code 34-1701 through 34-
1705, the Grangeville City Clerk shall have twenty (20) days from the date of
the filing of any petition to make certification to its correctness. (Ord. 516,
6-4-1979)
 
Notes
1 1. These provisions adopted pursuant to Idaho Code 31-717 as added by 1977
  Session Laws, chapter 145, page 321.
CHAPTER 10
COUNCIL RULES OF PROCEDURE
SECTION:
1-10-1: Meetings
1-10-2: Minutes
1-10-3: Presiding Officer
1-10-4: Council Members
1-10-5: Order Of Business
1-10-6: Motions
1-10-7: Consent Agenda Procedures
1-10-8: Public Testimony, Hearing Procedures, And Grievances
1-10-9: Ordinance And Resolution Procedures
1-10-10: Members Must Vote; Exceptions
1-10-11: Parliamentary Authority
1-10-1: MEETINGS:
   A.   Definitions:
EXECUTIVE SESSION: Any meeting or part of a meeting of the City Council which
is closed to any persons for deliberation on any of the below listed matters:
      1.   To consider hiring a public officer, employee, staff member or
individual agent, but not appointment to a vacancy in an elective office;
      2.   To consider the evaluation, dismissal, disciplining or hearing
complaints or charges against a public officer, employee, staff member or
agent;
      3.   To conduct deliberations concerning labor negotiations, or to
acquire an interest in real property which is not owned by a public agency;
      4.   To consider records that are exempt by law from public inspection;
      5.   To consider preliminary negotiations involving matters of trade or
commerce in which the City Council is in competition with governing bodies in
other governmental entities;
      6.   To consider and advise legal representatives in pending litigation
or where there is a general public awareness of probable litigation;
      7.   To conduct labor negotiations if either side requests closed
meetings.
MEETINGS: The convening of the City Council to make a decision or deliberate
toward a decision on any matter. "Decision" shall mean any determination,
action, vote or final disposition upon a motion, proposal, resolution, order,
ordinance or measure on which a vote of the Council is required, at any meeting
at which a quorum is present. "Deliberation" shall mean the receipt or exchange
of information or opinions relating to a decision, but shall not include
informal or impromptu discussions of a general nature which do not specifically
relate to a matter currently pending before the City Council.
QUORUM: The minimum number of members required to be present for the
transaction of business. A majority of the full Council shall constitute a
quorum. (Res. 169, 9-23-2002)
   B.   Regular Meetings: The Council shall hold regular meetings on the first
and third Mondays of each month pursuant to section
1-6-4 of this title. Meetings will be held at the Council Chambers,
Grangeville, Idaho. (Res. 169, 9-23-2002; amd. Ord. 927, 10-15-2018)
The City Council shall be permitted to change Council meetings to any day that
is not a state holiday, and additionally made by an affirmative vote of the
council present change meetings dates to the second and fourth Mondays of
months that include five (5) Mondays.
   C.   Special Meetings: A special meeting of the council may be called at any
time by the mayor or a majority of the members of the full council. Meeting and
agenda notice shall be made at least twenty four (24) hours prior to any
special meeting, unless an emergency exists. Items not included in the agenda
notice for special meetings shall not be considered or deliberated upon by the
council, unless an emergency exists.
   D.   Executive Sessions: Upon a two-thirds (2/3) vote of the full council,
the council shall meet in executive session, after the presiding officer has
identified the specific authorized purpose for the "executive session", as
defined in subsection A of this section. No executive session may be held for
the purpose of taking any final action or making any final decision.
   E.   Agenda Meetings: The council shall have the option, at the direction of
the mayor, to hold a meeting in advance of any council meeting, during which
time the agenda will be discussed, but no formal action will be taken and no
formal decisions made. The public is invited to all such agenda meetings.
   F.   Workshop Meetings: The council may, at the direction of the mayor, meet
for a workshop session, at which time no formal action may be taken, and
members of the public are always welcome to attend and if invited by the
council may participate to provide information to the council in such workshop
meetings. (Res. 169, 9-23-2002)
1-10-2: MINUTES:
The city clerk shall take written minutes of every meeting of the council.
Minutes shall contain the roll call of the council; all motions, resolutions,
orders, or ordinances proposed; the council members moving and seconding each
question; the disposition of each question; and the results of all votes.
Minutes shall include the motion and roll call vote to convene an executive
session, and the specific authorized purpose for the "executive session", as
defined in subsection
1-10-1A of this chapter. Minutes shall be available for public inspection
during normal office hours within a reasonable time after each meeting. (Res.
169, 9-23-2002)
1-10-3: PRESIDING OFFICER:
   A.   Definition: The "presiding officer" shall be the mayor, or in the
absence of the mayor, the council president shall preside over the meeting.
   B.   Duties: The presiding officer shall preserve order and decorum, shall
recognize every member who desires to speak, shall state all questions before
the council, may speak to points of order in preference to other members, and
shall respond to inquiries of the members. When two (2) or more members happen
to request recognition at once, the presiding officer shall name who is to
speak first. The presiding officer shall rule out of order any motions
obviously designed to frustrate the progress of business.
   C.   Questions Of Order: The presiding officer shall decide all questions of
order, which shall be subject to an appeal to the council, on which appeal no
member shall speak more than once without council approval. (Res. 169, 9-23-
2002)
1-10-4: COUNCIL MEMBERS:
   A.   Privileges: No member shall speak more than twice on the same question
until every member choosing to speak shall have spoken.
   B.   Addressing The Chair: When any member is about to speak in debate or
deliver any matter to the council, he shall respectfully address the presiding
officer, and shall confine himself to the question under debate and shall not
make personal comments or criticisms addressed to any individual. (Res. 169, 9-
23-2002)
1-10-5: ORDER OF BUSINESS:
   A.   Announcement Of Order: The presiding officer shall announce at each
meeting of the council the order of business, and no business shall be taken up
or considered until the class to which it belongs shall be declared in order.
All questions relating to the order of business shall be decided without
debate. The business of the council shall be presented in the following order:
      1.   Call to order.
      2.   Optional opening ceremony with the Pledge of Allegiance.
      3.   Roll call by the clerk.
      4.   Approval of meeting agenda.
      5.   Citizen issues and guests.
      6.   Committee reports.
      7.   Unfinished business.
      8.   New business.
      9.   Applications and communications to the council.
      10.   Adjournment.
   B.   Public Hearings: Public hearings may be scheduled at specific times any
time the council is in session and the hearing time shall take precedence over
the order of business described above. (Res. 169, 9-23-2002)
1-10-6: MOTIONS:
   A.   Motions During Debate: During the debate of a motion, only the
following motions are permissible:
      1.   To adjourn (nondebatable, nonamendable).
      2.   To lay on the table (nondebatable, nonamendable).
      3.   To postpone to a day certain (debatable, amendable).
      4.   To refer to a committee (debatable, amendable).
      5.   To amend (debatable, amendable).
      6.   To postpone indefinitely (debatable, nonamendable).
Multiple motions shall be decided in the above order.
   B.   Adjournment: A motion to adjourn shall always be in order, except when
the motion has been once made and voted down; the motion to adjourn shall not
again be in order until some other business shall have been taken up. A motion
to adjourn shall be always decided without debate.
   C.   Lay On The Table: A motion to lay on the table, that is, to temporarily
postpone a pending question during the meeting, shall be decided without
debate.
   D.   Reconsideration: When a question has been decided, any member who voted
in the majority, or any member in the case of a tie vote, may move for a
reconsideration of the vote. A motion to reconsider a vote is in order until
the adjournment of the next meeting of the council. A motion for
reconsideration may be made only once. (Res. 169, 9-23-2002)
1-10-7: CONSENT AGENDA PROCEDURES:
   A.   Definition: Items on the "consent agenda" are those considered routine
by the city clerk, including, but not limited to, the following items:
      1.   Grant deeds.
      2.   Grants of easements.
      3.   Auditors' reports as to cash count.
      4.   Call for bids and bid results.
      5.   Reports and minutes of administrative actions and proposals.
      6.   Leases and agreements previously approved in principle.
      7.   Claims against the city.
      8.   Approval of warrants and checks.
      9.   Approval of licenses and permits.
      10.   Scheduling of public hearings.
      11.   Certain resolutions.
      12.   Receipt and filing of minutes reports and requests of City boards
and commissions.
   B.   Consent Agenda Ordinance: The manner of dealing with the consent agenda
shall be as directed in section
1-6-6 of this title. (Res. 169, 9-23-2002)
1-10-8: PUBLIC TESTIMONY, HEARING PROCEDURES, AND GRIEVANCES:
   A.   All procedures shall be directed to providing participants in public
hearings a fair chance to be heard by the Council.
   B.   Public hearings before the Grangeville City Council and the Planning
and Zoning Commission, shall be as described in section
1-10-1 of this chapter, the terms and conditions of which are incorporated
herein as if set out in full. Grievance procedures and hearing before the City
Council, relating to employment matters, or disciplinary matters, are currently
set forth in the Grangeville Personnel Handbook, the terms and conditions of
which procedures are incorporated herein as if set out in full. Together with,
those additional directives that appear in Grangeville resolution 73 or any
amendments thereto, the terms and conditions of which are likewise incorporated
herein as if set out in full.
   C.   The presiding officer to all such hearings shall have the authority to
recognize participants in the hearing process and to maintain order in its
conduct. (Res. 169, 9-23-2002)
1-10-9: ORDINANCE AND RESOLUTION PROCEDURES:
   A.   Classifications: All actions of the Council involving the exercise of
the City's legislative and police power functions, or actions otherwise
required by law to be in ordinance form, shall be designated as ordinances and
appear in the form required by law. All other actions of the Council relating
to the administrative business of the City and requiring written findings or
statements shall be designated as resolutions.
   B.   Reading:
      1.   Ordinances: Prior to final passage, all ordinances shall be read on
three (3) different days, two (2) readings of which may be by title only and
one reading of which shall be in full, unless a majority of the members of the
full Council shall dispense with the rule.
      2.   Resolutions: Prior to final passage, all resolutions shall be read
on one day, the reading of which may be by title only.
   C.   Passage: The passage of every ordinance and resolution shall be by a
roll call of the Council with the yea or nay of each member present being
recorded. A quorum of the Council shall be required to make a decision on any
ordinance or resolution. (Res. 169, 9-23-2002)
1-10-10: MEMBERS MUST VOTE; EXCEPTIONS:
Every Council member present shall vote for or against each question put before
the Council, unless the Council shall excuse him. No member shall be permitted
to vote on a question when the yeas and nays are called for unless present when
his name is called in its regular order. No decision at any meeting of the
Council shall be made by secret ballot. (Res. 169, 9-23-2002)
1-10-11: PARLIAMENTARY AUTHORITY:
"Robert's Rules of Order Newly Revised" (most current edition) shall be the
authority in parliamentary matters not covered in this chapter. (Res. 169, 9-
23-2002)
CHAPTER 11
PUBLIC RECORDS
SECTION:
1-11-1: Definitions
1-11-2: Public Records; Public Access
1-11-3: Response To Request For Public Access
1-11-4: Appeal Of Denial To Public Records
1-11-5: Exempt Records
1-11-1: DEFINITIONS:
CITY: City of Grangeville.
CUSTODIAN: The person having personal custody and control of the public records
and shall refer to the City Clerk and his or her designee.
EXEMPT: The custodian is free from the obligation to disclose public records.
INSPECT: The right to listen, view, and make notes of public records as long as
the public record is not altered or damaged.
PUBLIC RECORD: Includes, but is not limited to, any writing containing
information relating to the conduct or administration of the public's business
prepared, owned, used or retained by the City regardless of physical form or
characteristics.
WRITING: Includes, but is not limited to, hand writing, type writing, printing,
photostating, photographing, and every means of recording, including letters,
words, pictures, sounds or symbols, or combination thereof, and all papers,
maps, magnetic or paper tapes, photographic films and prints, magnetic or
punched cards, discs, drums or other documents. (Ord. 633, 10-21-1991)
1-11-2: PUBLIC RECORDS; PUBLIC ACCESS:
All public records of the City shall be open and available to the general
public during the hours of nine o'clock (9:00) A.M. to eleven forty five
o'clock (11:45) A.M. and one fifteen o'clock (1:15) P.M. through four thirty
o'clock (4:30) P.M. Monday through Friday, except declared holidays.
Any individual seeking public records shall make their request to the
custodian, or his designee, during the above stated hours. Every individual
shall have the right to inspect and every effort will be made to facilitate
this right. However, nothing shall prevent the custodian from maintaining such
vigilance to prevent alteration of any public record. A written request will be
required if the record desired is not readily available or identifiable by the
custodian, or his designee. (Ord. 633, 10-21-1991)
Any individual seeking copies of public records may utilize their own
equipment, however, public records shall not be removed from City Hall. Copies
of public records may be made upon City copying equipment at a rate as
established in the master fee schedule. (Ord. 633, 10-21-1991; amd. Ord. 925,
10-1-2018)
Public records may be inspected outside of the above stated hours if requested
in writing with said request being made in advance. The person requesting said
inspection will be responsible for compensation to the City at the cost of said
inspection.
Where it is in the public interest to do so, the Mayor, any City Council
member, or any supervisory employee, or the custodian may waive any fee
required in this Chapter. (Ord. 633, 10-21-1991)
1-11-3: RESPONSE TO REQUEST FOR PUBLIC ACCESS:
Every individual seeking to inspect the public record shall either be granted
or denied the right within three (3) working days of the request. If the
custodian determines that more time is needed to locate or retrieve the public
records, the custodian shall notify the person requesting to inspect the public
records of said delay, in writing. In no event shall the delay extend later
than ten (10) working days.
If the custodian fails to respond to the request it shall be deemed denied
within ten (10) working days following the request or if the request is deemed
denied then notice of denial will be reviewed by the City Attorney and shall
state the statutory authority for the denial and indicate the person's right to
appeal the denial. (Ord. 633, 10-21-1991)
1-11-4: APPEAL OF DENIAL TO PUBLIC RECORDS:
Any individual aggrieved by the denial of a request for disclosure of public
records may institute proceeding in District Court to compel the City to make
the records available pursuant to law. (Ord. 633, 10-21-1991)
1-11-5: EXEMPT RECORDS:
The following records are exempt from disclosure:
   A.   Any public record exempt from disclosure by Federal or State law or
Federal regulations to the extent specifically provided for by such law or
regulation.
   B.   Production records, sale or purchase records, cash records, mortgage
portfolio loan documents, or similar business records of a private concern or
enterprise required by law to be submitted to or inspected by a public agency.
Nothing in this subsection shall limit the use which can be made of such
information for regulatory purposes or its admissibility in any enforcement
proceeding.
   C.   Records relating to the appraisal of real property, timber, or mineral
rights prior to its acquisition, sale or lease by a public agency.
   D.   Any estimate prepared by a public agency that details the cost of a
public project until such time as disclosed or bids are opened, or upon award
of the contract for construction of the public project.
   E.   Test questions, scoring keys, and other data used to administer a
licensing examination, employment, academic or other examination or testing
procedure before the examination is given if the examination is to be used
again. Records establishing procedures for and instructing persons
administering, grading or evaluating an examination or testing procedure are
included in this exemption, to the extent that disclosure would create a risk
that the result might be affected.
   F.   Retired employees' and retired public officials' home addresses, home
telephone numbers and other financial and nonfinancial membership records;
active employee financial and membership records and mortgage portfolio loan
documents maintained by the public employee retirement system. Financial
statements prepared by retirement system staff, funding agents and custodians
concerning the investment of assets of the public employee retirement system of
Idaho are not considered confidential under this Chapter.
   G.   Any personal records, other than names and addresses, such as
parentage, race, religion, sex, height, weight, tax identification and social
security numbers, financial worth or medical condition submitted to any public
agency pursuant to a statutory requirement for licensing, certification, permit
or bonding.
   H.   Unless otherwise provided by agency rule, information obtained as part
of any inquiry into a person's fitness to be granted or retain a license,
certificate, permit, privilege, commission or position.
   I.   Employment security information and unemployment insurance benefit
information, except that all interested parties may agree to waive the
exemption.
   J.   Investigatory records of a law enforcement agency, as defined in Idaho
Code 9-337(5), under the conditions set forth in Idaho Code 9-335.
   K.   Records of a personal nature related directly or indirectly to the
application for and provision of statutory services rendered to persons
applying for public care for the elderly, indigent, or mentally or physically
handicapped, or participation in an environmental or a public health study.
   L.   Records of hospital care, medical records, records of psychiatric care
or treatment and professional counseling records relating to an individual's
condition, diagnosis, care or treatment.
   M.   Records of a person maintained pursuant to Idaho Code, title 16,
chapter 18.
   N.   Except as provided in this subsection, all personnel records of a
current or former public official other than the public official's public
service or employment history, classification, pay grade and step, longevity,
gross salary and salary history, status, workplace and employing agency. All
other personnel information relating to a public employee or applicant,
including, but not limited to, information regarding sex, race, marital status,
birth date, home address and telephone number, applications, testing and
scoring materials, grievances, correspondence and performance evaluations,
shall not be disclosed to the public without the employee's or applicant's
written consent. A public official or authorized representative may inspect and
copy his personnel records, except for material used to screen and test for
employment.
   O.   Written communications between the City Attorney and the Mayor, City
Council members and department heads when such records constitute
communications within the scope of the attorney-client relationship.
   P.   Any written agendas, information sheets, handouts, notes or minutes of
duly authorized executive meetings of the City Council. (Ord. 633, 10-21-1991)
TITLE 2
BOARDS AND COMMISSIONS
CHAPTER 1
PLANNING AND ZONING COMMISSION
SECTION:
2-1-1: Commission Created; Members
2-1-2: Authority
2-1-3: Rules And Regulations
2-1-1: COMMISSION CREATED; MEMBERS:
   A.   Creation; Membership: There is hereby created a commission to be known
and designated as the planning and zoning commission. Such planning and zoning
commission shall consist of seven (7) voting members residing either within or
without the city of Grangeville, but interested in Grangeville's welfare. The
seven (7) members mentioned above shall be appointed by the mayor with the
approval of the city council, and no longer shall one of the members of the
commission be a city council person. Furthermore, one member of the planning
and zoning commission shall be appointed as the area of city impact
representative pursuant to section
10-9-7 of this code, as amended.
   B.   Terms Of Office: On the taking effect of this chapter, the mayor shall
appoint one representative of the planning and zoning commission from the area
of city impact to hold a three (3) year term. As to the other six (6) members,
two (2) shall be appointed for terms of one year, two (2) shall be appointed
for terms of two (2) years, and two (2) shall be appointed for terms of three
(3) years respectively. Thereafter as the term of each member expires, the
mayor shall fill vacancies for three (3) year terms. Any commissioner may be
removed from office at any time by the mayor with the concurrence of a majority
of the city council, except as it relates to the representative from the area
of city impact when additionally, the concurrence of the county commissioners
will likewise be required. Members of the board shall serve without salary but
may receive their actual and necessary budgeted expenses while engaged in
authorized business of the planning and zoning commission. Members that are
appointed to fill vacancies shall be appointed so that their terms are
staggered as herein required.
   C.   Clerk Of The Commission: The planning and zoning commission shall
designate a person who shall be an ex officio clerk of the planning and zoning
commission and keep its records and notify it of the filing of applications for
permits and such other matters that shall come before the commission.
   D.   Meetings: When there is business to transact, the commission shall hold
a meeting at least once each month, or more often, as the business of the
commission requires. (Ord. 794, 12-5-2005)
2-1-2: AUTHORITY:
The commission shall specifically have that authority that is granted to it, by
the Idaho local planning act, and is otherwise delegated to it by either the
city council or the provisions of this code, which is Idaho Code, title 67,
chapter 65. (Ord. 687, 7-8-1996)
2-1-3: RULES AND REGULATIONS:
The planning and zoning commission shall adopt such rules and regulations as it
may deem necessary, pursuant to the revisions of Idaho Code, title 67, chapter
65, to carry into effect the provisions and purposes of this chapter. It shall
hold such meetings and meet at such places as from time to time shall be
necessary and it shall hold such hearings as the commission or the majority
thereof, or the law may require. At the first meeting of the commission in
January of each year, it shall elect one of its members as chairman, and each
day thereafter, during the first meeting in January, the commission shall again
select a chairman for the next succeeding year. (Ord. 687, 7-8-1996)
CHAPTER 2
LIBRARY BOARD
SECTION:
2-2-1: Library, Creation
2-2-2: Board Appointment And Term
2-2-3: Rules; Elect Officers
2-2-4: Use Of Library Room
2-2-5: Reports Of Board
2-2-6: Donations For Library
2-2-7: Funds For Operation
2-2-8: Removal Of Library Trustees
2-2-9: Fee For Nonresident Use
2-2-10: Library Operational Fees
2-2-1: LIBRARY, CREATION:
A public library and reading room is hereby established under and by virtue of
the provisions of this chapter. (1959 Code)
2-2-2: BOARD APPOINTMENT AND TERM:
Library trustees shall be appointed and serve terms pursuant to Title 33,
Chapter 26, Idaho Code. (Ord. 486, 12-20-1976; amd. Ord. 974, 1-2-2024)
2-2-3: RULES; ELECT OFFICERS:
Said trustees shall immediately after their appointment, meet and organize, by
the election of one of their members as president and by the election of such
officers as they shall deem necessary. They shall make and adopt such rules,
bylaws and regulations for their own guidance and for the government of the
library and the reading room as may be expedient. The city council shall have
the final control of the expenditures and all monies collected for the library
fund, but the library board shall advise and recommend to the city council,
which expenditures from time to time shall be appropriate and necessary for the
care and custody of the library or any necessary function of the library.
The library board, subject to the approval of the city council may appoint a
librarian and such other assistants as shall be deemed necessary and prescribe
rules for their conduct. (Ord. 574, 5-7-1984)
2-2-4: USE OF LIBRARY ROOM:
The library and reading room hereby established shall be forever free for the
use of the inhabitants of the city; always subject to such reasonable rules and
regulations as the library board may find necessary to adopt and publish in
order to render the use of the library and reading room of the greatest benefit
to the greatest number and they may exclude and cut off from the use of said
library and reading room any and all persons who shall wilfully violate such
rules. (1959 Code)
2-2-5: REPORTS OF BOARD:
Said board of trustees, or their designee, shall make a quarterly report at the
first meeting of the city council in the months of May, August, November and
February of each year to summarize the activities of the library in the last
quarter with such other statistics and information and suggestions as it may
deem of general interest and the City Council may require. (1959 Code; amd.
Ord. 486, 12-20-1976; Ord. 974, 1-2-2024)
2-2-6: DONATIONS FOR LIBRARY:
All persons desirous of making donations of money, personal property, or real
estate for the benefit of the library may vest title to the same in the City,
to be controlled by the City Council, under the advice and recommendation of
the Library Board.
   A.   Should any donation to the library, be specific as to how such donation
should be used, the City Council shall be bound by those specific restrictions.
   B.   In the event a donation is granted to the library without specific
directions, the same shall be separately accounted for in a fund to be known as
the Library Memorial Fund. Such fund may be used by the City Council with the
advice and recommendation of the board for the purchase of books, magazines, or
equipment, or any other capital improvement other than items required for the
normal operation of the library, and shall not be used for salaries. (Ord. 573,
5-7-1984)
2-2-7: FUNDS FOR OPERATION:
There is hereby created a special fund to be known as the Library Fund, which
shall be kept by the City Treasurer separate and apart from other monies of the
City to be used exclusively for the purchase of books, periodicals, necessary
furniture and fixtures and compensation for a librarian and assistant and
whatever is required for the maintenance of such library and reading room and
all monies for the use and benefit of said library shall be kept in said
Library Fund. (1959 Code)
2-2-8: REMOVAL OF LIBRARY TRUSTEES:
Removal of library trustees shall be conducted pursuant to Title 33, Chapter
26, Idaho Code. (1959 Code; amd. Ord. 974, 1-2-2024)
2-2-9: FEE FOR NONRESIDENT USE:
The City Council shall have the right to fix a fee for the use of the
Grangeville Municipal Library by nonresidents. Such fee for nonresident use
shall be as established in the master fee schedule. Such fee as now adopted, or
as shall be hereafter amended, shall entitle the card holder to one full year
of library use beginning on the date of issuance and continuing for one full
year thereafter. Upon the purchase of such nonresident family library card,
that family shall be entitled to use the Grangeville Municipal Library in the
same manner as City residents might or could do. A library card shall bear on
its face its expiration date and may be renewed for the next full year after
payment of the fee as established in the master fee schedule. (Ord. 742, 10-22-
2001; amd. Ord. 925, 10-1-2018)
The library staff shall maintain accurate records reflecting the issuance of
each nonresident family library card as from time to time may be issued or
renewed.
All receipts received by the library on account of such nonresident library
card shall be kept by the City Clerk in the Library Fund pursuant to section
2-2-7 of this chapter.
A "nonresident" shall be defined as any person and his or her family
maintaining his or her usual place of abode outside of the incorporated limits
of the City. However, in the event such person living outside of the
incorporated limits owns property within the City limits he or she would be
considered a resident. It shall be the responsibility of any property owner
claiming residency under this definition to provide adequate proof to the
Library Director as to property ownership within the City. (Ord. 742, 10-22-
2001)
2-2-10: LIBRARY OPERATIONAL FEES:
Library operational fees charged to the public shall be as established in the
master fee schedule. (Ord. 733, 4-2-2001; amd. Ord. 925, 10-1-2018)
CHAPTER 3
RECREATION COMMISSION
SECTION:
2-3-1: Establishment; Term Of Office
2-3-2: Rules And Regulations
2-3-3: Annual Budget
2-3-4: Reports
2-3-5: Advisory Commission Only
2-3-1: ESTABLISHMENT; TERM OF OFFICE:
There is hereby created a Recreation Commission for the City. The Commission
shall consist of four (4) members who shall receive no salary. They shall be
appointed by the Mayor and confirmed by the City Council. The members shall be
chosen from the residents of the City. The term of office of each member shall
be for a term of two (2) years or until his successor is appointed and
qualified. Vacancies in such Commission occurring otherwise than by expiration
of the term shall be filled by the Mayor for the unexpired term. (1959 Code)
2-3-2: RULES AND REGULATIONS:
Immediately after the appointment of the members of the Recreation Commission
they shall meet and organize by electing one of their members president and
such other officers as may be necessary. The Commission shall have the power to
adopt bylaws, rules and regulations for the proper conduct of the public parks
and recreation in and for the City. Said bylaws, rules and regulations are
subject to the approval of the Mayor and City Council.
The Recreation Commission shall provide conduct of and the supervision of
public parks and public playgrounds, athletic fields, recreation centers,
recreational facilities and other recreation activities on any of the
properties owned or controlled by the City, or on other properties with the
consent of the owners and occupants thereof. It shall have the power to conduct
any form of recreation or cultural activities that will employ the leisure time
of the people in a constructive and wholesome manner.
The Recreation Commission shall have the power to appoint or designate someone
to act as Superintendent, who is trained and properly qualified for the work
and such other personnel as the Commission deems proper, subject to the
approval of the Mayor and City Council. (1959 Code)
2-3-3: ANNUAL BUDGET:
The Recreation Commission shall submit annually a budget to the Mayor and
Council of the City for their approval. The Commission may also solicit or
receive any gifts or bequests of money, or other personal property or any
donation, principal or income, for either temporary or permanent use for public
playgrounds or other recreational purposes. Said property and/or gifts,
however, to be and remain the property of the City. (1959 Code)
2-3-4: REPORTS:
The Recreation Commission shall make full and complete monthly and annual
reports to the Mayor and Council of the City and other reports from time to
time as requested by the Mayor and City Council. (1959 Code)
2-3-5: ADVISORY COMMISSION ONLY:
The Recreation Commission shall not be deemed to be other than an advisory
commission to advise the Mayor and City Council. (1959 Code)
CHAPTER 4
SKI COURSE BOARD
(Rep. by Ord. 900, 7-6-2015)
CHAPTER 5
TRAFFIC SAFETY COMMISSION
SECTION:
2-5-1: Creation
2-5-2: Membership And Terms Of Office
2-5-3: Vacancies
2-5-4: Organization
2-5-5: Meetings
2-5-6: Duties
2-5-1: CREATION:
There is hereby created and established a commission to be known as GRANGEVILLE
TRAFFIC SAFETY COMMISSION. (Ord. 407, 11-3-1969)
2-5-2: MEMBERSHIP AND TERMS OF OFFICE:
The Traffic Safety Commission shall consist of eight (8) members to be
appointed by the Mayor, with the consent and approval of the City Council.
Members of said Commission shall hold office for a period of six (6) years each
and said terms shall be staggered in such a manner so that the terms of not
more than three (3) members shall expire in any one year. Two (2) of such
members shall hold office for a term of two (2) years, three (3) shall hold
office for a term of four (4) years and three (3) for six (6) years, the
respective terms of office to be determined by lot at the first meeting of the
Commission. Thereafter the term of office for each appointive member shall be
six (6) years.
Members shall be selected so that there shall always remain in the Commission
one Public Works Director, one City Judge or Magistrate, one Chief of Police,
one City Attorney, one local citizen, two (2) City Councilmen, and the Mayor of
the City, and shall serve without compensation. (Ord. 407, 11-3-1969)
2-5-3: VACANCIES:
Vacancies shall be filled by appointment of the Mayor, with the consent of the
City Council. (Ord. 407, 11-3-1969)
2-5-4: ORGANIZATION:
The Commission shall elect its own chairman and secretary and create and fill
such other offices as it may determine necessary, and adopt such rules as it
shall deem necessary to carry out its purpose. (Ord. 407, 11-3-1969)
2-5-5: MEETINGS:
The Commission shall hold one regular meeting each month for not less than nine
(9) months in each year. A majority of the appointive members of the Commission
shall be necessary to constitute a quorum at any meeting. All meetings shall be
open to the public. A written record of its meetings, resolutions, findings,
and determinations shall be kept, which shall be a public record.
The Commission may require the attendance at any meeting of such other City
officials as it may deem necessary. (Ord. 407, 11-3-1969)
2-5-6: DUTIES:
It shall be the duty of the Commission to recommend and make suggestions to the
City Council for the adoption of plans for traffic safety as recommended by the
National Safety Council Study of 1968; to coordinate all City traffic safety
plans into the State plan; to make suggestions for projects designed to
increase safety in pedestrian and school traffic in the City and to generally
recommend to the City Council plans to improve traffic safety in the entire
City. (Ord. 407, 11-3-1969)
CHAPTER 6
BOARD OF HEALTH
SECTION:
2-6-1: Board Of Health Created; Personnel
2-6-2: Appointment Of Board; Term Of Office
2-6-3: Powers Of Board
2-6-4: Mayor As Chairman Of Board
2-6-5: Quorum
2-6-1: BOARD OF HEALTH CREATED; PERSONNEL:
A Board of Health for the City of Grangeville is hereby created to consist of
the following members:
The Mayor, one other member of the City Council and one other citizen of the
City. Provided that one member of said Board of Health shall be a regularly
licensed and practicing physician within the City. (1959 Code)
2-6-2: APPOINTMENT OF BOARD; TERM OF OFFICE:
The members of the Board of Health shall be appointed by the Mayor with
approval of the City Council and shall hold their office until their successors
are appointed and qualify. (1959 Code)
2-6-3: POWERS OF BOARD:
Said Board of Health or any member or members delegated therefrom, shall have
power to examine private premises as well as public in the interests of the
health of the City, and, if deemed by said Board necessary to cause any and all
premises, buildings or other place or places, to be cleaned or disinfected or
both, and to adopt and enforce rules and regulations of a sanitary character
that the said Board may deem necessary, and they shall have such power and
authority as is delegated by the laws of the State of Idaho to the boards of
health of like degree. (1959 Code)
2-6-4: MAYOR AS CHAIRMAN OF BOARD:
The Mayor shall be chairman of the Board of Health and shall have power to call
the Board together at any and all times and in case of his absence, inability
or refusal so to act, then the other members may call and hold meetings.
Provided that the minutes of such meeting shall show the absence, inability or
refusal of the chairman to call such meeting. (1959 Code)
2-6-5: QUORUM:
A majority of said Board shall constitute a quorum for the transaction of any
and all business of said Board. (1959 Code)
TITLE 3
DEPARTMENTS
CHAPTER 1
POLICE DEPARTMENT
SECTION:
3-1-1: Department Created
3-1-2: Chief Of Police
3-1-3: Departmental Duties
3-1-4: Serve As Witnesses
3-1-5: Rules And Regulations
3-1-6: Matrons
3-1-7: Rewards
3-1-1: DEPARTMENT CREATED:
There is hereby created a Police Department which shall consist of the Chief of
Police and such other personnel as may be provided by the governing body of the
City. (1959 Code)
3-1-2: CHIEF OF POLICE:
   A.   Appointment: The Chief of Police shall be appointed by the Mayor
subject to the approval of the City Council. He shall hold office for the
duration of his appointment unless sooner removed by the Mayor with a
concurrence of the City Council.
   B.   Rank: The Chief of Police shall be the head of the Department and have
supervision over all the officers and members thereof. The Chief of Police may,
with the approval of the Mayor, appoint such special police as may be required
from time to time, however, such appointment may not be for a period of longer
than ten (10) days and special police shall not be reappointed following the
specified ten (10) days without the consent of the governing body.
   C.   Duties Of Chief: The Chief of Police shall keep such records and make
such reports concerning the activities of his Department as may be required by
statute or by the Mayor. He shall be responsible for the performance of the
Police Department and of its functions and all persons who are members of the
Police Department shall serve subject to his orders.
It shall be the duty of the Chief of Police to see to the enforcement of all
provisions of this Code and of all applicable statutes and to preserve order
and prevent infractions of the law and arrest violators thereof. He shall have
authority to call upon any citizen or bystander to assist him in the execution
of his duty. He shall serve all processes issued to him and enforce all orders
and judgments of the court.
   D.   Stolen Property: The Chief of Police shall have the custody of all
lost, abandoned or stolen property recovered within the City. (1959 Code)
3-1-3: DEPARTMENTAL DUTIES:
It shall be the duty of the members of the Police Department to see to the
enforcement of all of the laws of the City and all statutes applicable therein;
and to preserve order and prevent infractions of the law and arrest violators
thereof. (1959 Code)
3-1-4: SERVE AS WITNESSES:
Every member of the Police Department shall appear as witness whenever
necessary in a prosecution for a violation of any law or of any State or
Federal law. No such member shall retain any witness fee for service as witness
in any action or suit to which the City is a party; any fees paid for such
services shall be turned over to the Chief of Police, who shall deposit the
same with the City Treasurer. (1959 Code)
3-1-5: RULES AND REGULATIONS:
The Chief of the Police Department may make or prescribe such rules and
regulations as he shall deem advisable; such rules, when approved by the
governing body, shall be binding on such members. Such rules and regulations
may cover, besides the conduct of the members, uniforms and equipment to be
worn or carried, hours of service, vocations and all other similar matters
necessary or desirable for the better efficiency of the Department. (1959 Code)
3-1-6: MATRONS:
The Mayor, with the consent of the City Council, may appoint a police matron,
who shall perform such duties as may be assigned to her by the Chief of Police
or by the Mayor. (1959 Code)
3-1-7: REWARDS:
The Chief of Police, for meritorious service rendered by any member of the
police force in the due discharge of his duty, may permit such member to retain
for his own benefit, so far as he may be permitted by law, any reward or
present tendered him therefor, and it shall be cause of removal for any member
of the force to receive any such reward or present without notice thereof to
the Chief of Police and without his permission. (1959 Code)
CHAPTER 2
FIRE DEPARTMENT
SECTION:
3-2-1: Department Created
3-2-2: Fire Chief
3-2-3: Departmental Duties
3-2-4: Fire Prevention
3-2-5: Volunteer Members
3-2-1: DEPARTMENT CREATED:
There is hereby created a Fire Department which shall consist of a Fire Chief
and such other personnel as may be provided for by the governing body of the
City. (1959 Code)
3-2-2: FIRE CHIEF:
   A.   Appointment: The Chief of the Fire Department shall be appointed by the
Mayor subject to the approval of the City Council. He shall hold office for the
duration of his appointment unless sooner removed by the Mayor with the
concurrence of the City Council.
   B.   Rank: The Chief of the Fire Department, commonly referred to as the
Fire Chief, shall be the head of the Department and have supervision over all
officers and members thereof. The Fire Chief may, with the approval of the
Mayor, appoint such other Fire Department officers as may be deemed necessary,
including a First Assistant Chief and a Second Assistant Chief.
   C.   Duties: The Fire Chief shall keep such records and make such reports
concerning the activities of his Department as may be required by statute or by
the Mayor. He shall be responsible for the performance of the Fire Department
and of its functions and all persons who are members of the Fire Department
shall serve subject to his orders. He shall be responsible for the control and
custody of all Fire Department property and equipment. He shall have the
authority of a police officer while actively engaged in fighting a fire, or
going to or from a fire. (1959 Code)
3-2-3: DEPARTMENTAL DUTIES:
It shall be the duty of members of the Fire Department to provide for the
immediate answering of all fire calls and to fight all fires in the best and
most modern available methods. Members shall see to the care and maintenance of
all fire fighting equipment and have such equipment in constant workable
condition at all times. (1959 Code)
3-2-4: FIRE PREVENTION:
Every possible action shall be taken by the members of the Fire Department to
eliminate fire hazards and to provide for fire prevention methods and
operations within the City. (1959 Code)
3-2-5: VOLUNTEER MEMBERS:
Any volunteer members of the Fire Department shall conduct themselves in the
same manner and under the same rules and regulations as regular members of the
Department. They shall respond to all fire calls according to a schedule
prescribed by the Chief of the Fire Department and they shall attend all
meetings and drills called by the Chief. (1959 Code)
CHAPTER 3
WATER DEPARTMENT
SECTION:
3-3-1: Water Superintendent
3-3-1: WATER SUPERINTENDENT:
The Water Superintendent shall have general supervision over the waterworks of
said City, and appurtenances thereto, under the direction of the Mayor and City
Council. Said Superintendent shall attend to the tapping of mains, and laying
and connecting up of laterals and installation of meters and meter boxes, and
shall see that all open ditches and excavations on or along the streets, alleys
and thoroughfares of said City are carefully guarded by rails and lights or
other proper warning signals. He shall have charge of and operate the pumping
stations and reservoirs and shall keep the mains of said system filled with
pure and wholesome water at a pressure sufficient for proper fire protection.
Said Superintendent shall also keep an inventory of all property belonging to
the water system and shall, with the consent of the Mayor and City Council,
purchase supplies and equipment necessary for the maintenance of the system. He
shall, upon request, attend meetings of the City Council and render such
reports and statements as may be required, he shall perform such other duties
as may be required of him by law or order of the Mayor or City Council, and to
the end that the provisions of this Section may be carried out, the said
Superintendent shall be allowed such assistance as the Mayor or City Council
may deem necessary and proper. (1959 Code)
TITLE 4
BUILDING REGULATIONS
CHAPTER 0
GENERAL REQUIREMENTS
SECTION:
4-0-1: Contractor Registration Number
4-0-1: CONTRACTOR REGISTRATION NUMBER:
No building permit will be issued without the contractor's registration number
being presented by the contractor, except when the permit applicant provides
evidence to the satisfaction of the building inspector or the city clerk or
their designee that the applicant is exempt from the registration requirements
pursuant to title 54, chapter 52, Idaho Code. (Ord. 795, 1-23-2006)
CHAPTER 1
BUILDING CODES
SECTION:
4-1-1: Adoption Of Codes
4-1-1: ADOPTION OF CODES:
   A.   Code Adoption: The approved editions of the following nationally
recognized codes, as adopted by the state of Idaho or the Idaho building code
board, are adopted as the official building codes of the city of Grangeville,
except as provided in subsection B of this section:
      1.   International building code;
      2.   International residential code, parts I–IV and part IX;
      3.   International energy conservation code;
      4.   Uniform code for the abatement of dangerous buildings, 1997 edition;
and
      5.   Uniform sign code, 1979 edition.
The adopted versions of the foregoing codes shall be deemed superseded by
successive versions of such codes as they are adopted or approved by the Idaho
building code board effective on any date such codes are made effective by the
Idaho building code board.
   B.   Exemptions: Agricultural buildings are exempt from the building codes
adopted herein, but shall remain subject to placement requirements established
by Grangeville city zoning regulations. (Ord. 783, 6-6-2005)
   C.   Building Permit Fees:
      1.   Before issuing a building permit the owner, or his agent, shall pay
the requisite fee to the city of Grangeville. The owner, or his agent, shall
also pay any other fees charged to the city of Grangeville from other
government entities for reviewing plans or permits. Fees charged are in
addition to the building permit fee and are required to be paid at the time of
the application. No permit shall be issued until all requisite fees are paid in
full.
      2.   Upon failure to obtain a permit before work on a building has begun,
except in emergency cases, the total fee shall be double the permit fees
charged.
      3.   There shall be no refunds once a permit has been issued. (Ord. 874,
5-7-2012)
   D.   Copies On File: The city clerk shall be authorized pursuant to Idaho
Code section 50-901 to maintain at least one copy of each of the codes adopted
in this section in her office available to public inspection. (Ord. 783, 6-6-
2005)
CHAPTER 2
PLUMBING CODE
SECTION:
4-2-1: Adoption Of Plumbing Code
4-2-1: ADOPTION OF PLUMBING CODE:
There is hereby adopted for the purpose of establishing minimum standards of
design, materials and workmanship for all plumbing hereafter installed, altered
or repaired and to establish methods of procedure with the limits of the City,
that certain plumbing code known as "National Plumbing Code" published by the
American Society of Mechanical Engineers, being particularly the most current
edition thereof, and the whole thereof, of which not less than three (3) copies
have been and now are filed in the office of the City Clerk and the same is
hereby adopted and incorporated as fully as though set out at length herein.
(Ord. 347, 12-4-1961)
CHAPTER 2
PLUMBING CODE
SECTION:
4-2-1: Adoption Of Plumbing Code
4-2-1: ADOPTION OF PLUMBING CODE:
There is hereby adopted for the purpose of establishing minimum standards of
design, materials and workmanship for all plumbing hereafter installed, altered
or repaired and to establish methods of procedure with the limits of the City,
that certain plumbing code known as the Idaho State Plumbing Code, being
particularly the most current edition thereof, and the whole thereof, of which
not less than one (1) copy has been and now is filed in the office of the City
Clerk and the same is hereby adopted and incorporated as fully as though set
out at length herein. (Ord. 347, 12-4-1961; amd. Ord. 956, 4-18-2022)
CHAPTER 3
ELECTRICAL CODE
SECTION:
4-3-1: Scope Of Code
4-3-2: Minimum Safety Standards
4-3-3: Special Requirements
4-3-4: Alterations To Existing Wiring
4-3-5: Electrical Inspector
4-3-6: Jurisdiction Of Electrical Inspector
4-3-7: Authority To Disconnect
4-3-8: Electrical Inspection Tags
4-3-9: State License Required
4-3-10: Liability Of City
4-3-11: Penalty For Violations
4-3-1: SCOPE OF CODE:
The regulations of this Code shall apply to all electrical wiring and equipment
installed within the corporate limits of the City, except wiring and equipment
which is used for the generation, control, distribution or communication system
of a utility and which is installed by or for, and owned and maintained by an
electrical or communication utility operating under due authority granted by
the City. Electrical wiring in Federal buildings, railway cars or automotive
equipment is exempt from the requirements of this Code. (Ord. 357, 4-1-1963)
4-3-2: MINIMUM SAFETY STANDARDS:
Except as herein provided all installations of wires and equipment to convey
electric current and apparatus to be operated by such current, made after the
effective date of this Code, shall be in compliance with the most current
Edition of the National Electrical Code, as provided by the American Standards
Association, relating to such work so far as the same covers both fire and
personal injury hazards, and as the National Electrical Code shall be amended,
revised, compiled and published from time to time and as such amendments or
revisions are adopted by the City Council. One (1) copy of the National
Electrical Code as adopted shall be kept on file in the office of the City
Clerk for use and examination of the public. (Ord. 671, 11-7-1994; amd. Ord.
956, 4-18-2022)
4-3-3: SPECIAL REQUIREMENTS:
All public, commercial and industrial buildings of any kind or description,
including apartment buildings located within the fire zone shall be wired to
conform in all respects with the National Electrical Code now in existence or
as hereafter amended. (Ord. 571, 2-21-1984)
4-3-4: ALTERATIONS TO EXISTING WIRING:
When extensions and/or alterations are made to any electrical circuit in or on
any buildings or structure, coming under the provisions of this Code and/or the
ordinances of the City, said electrical circuit, in its entirety, shall be made
to conform to such provisions of this Code as are particularly applicable
thereto. (Ord. 357, 4-1-1963)
4-3-5: ELECTRICAL INSPECTOR:
The Mayor is hereby authorized and directed to enter into an agreement with the
Idaho State Electrical Board, Department of Law Enforcement, to furnish
electrical inspection service to the City as authorized by Idaho Code 54-1001C
by a duly appointed State Electrical Inspector acting as Electrical Inspector
for the City. (Ord. 357, 4-1-1963)
4-3-6: JURISDICTION OF ELECTRICAL INSPECTOR:
Except as herein provided the installation of electrical wiring or equipment in
or on any building or structure within the corporate limits of the City, shall
be done at all times subject to the inspection by the Electrical Inspector of
the City. (Ord. 357, 4-1-1963)
4-3-7: AUTHORITY TO DISCONNECT:
If an electrical installation made after the effective date of this Code is
found to be defective or defectively installed, or otherwise not in conformity
with this Code the Electrical Inspector may order such installation
disconnected from the source of supply until the necessary corrections have
been made, provided that the owner of the premises, the tenant, if any, and the
power supply company shall be notified in writing. (Ord. 357, 4-1-1963)
4-3-8: ELECTRICAL INSPECTION TAGS:
   A.   It shall be unlawful for any person to install or cause to be
installed, any electrical wiring, or equipment coming under the provisions of
this Code unless an electrical inspection tag, as authorized by Idaho Code 54-
1005, or any application for such electrical inspection tag, properly
completed, has been mailed to the Idaho State Electrical Board, State House,
Boise, Idaho. Electrical contractors shall use the standard electrical
contractors inspection tags issued to all licensed electrical contractors by
the Idaho State Electrical Board. Owners installing electrical wiring or
equipment on their own property shall use the standard application for owners'
electrical inspection tag which applications shall be made available at the
Office of the City Clerk and at the local offices of the power suppliers.
   B.   The power supplier shall not connect to or energize any electrical
installation coming under the provisions of this Code unless such power
supplier has in possession, an electrical inspection tag, issued by the Idaho
State Electrical Board, covering the installation to be authorized. (Ord. 357,
4-1-1963)
4-3-9: STATE LICENSE REQUIRED:
   A.   Except as herein provided it shall be unlawful for any person to
perform or supervise the actual physical work of installing electric wires or
equipment to convey electric current unless such person holds a valid
journeyman electricians license, issued by the Idaho State Electrical Board,
Department of Law Enforcement.
   B.   Except as herein provided it shall be unlawful for any person,
partnership, company, association or corporation to engage in the business of
installing electrical wires or equipment to convey electrical current or to
enter into agreements to install such wires or equipment without a valid
electrical contractors license issued by the Idaho State Electrical Board,
Department of Law Enforcement.
Exemptions: The licensing provisions of this section shall not apply to persons
making electrical installations on their own property, to apprentice
electricians working under the direct, on the job, supervision of licensed
journeymen electricians nor to persons regularly employed to do electrical
maintenance work on their employer's premises. (Ord. 357, 4-1-1963)
4-3-10: LIABILITY OF CITY:
This Code is not to be construed to relieve from or lesson responsibility or
liability of any party owning, operating, or controlling, or installing any
electrical wiring or equipment, for damages to person or property caused by any
defects therein, nor shall the City be held as assuming any such liability by
reason of the inspection required herein. (Ord. 357, 4-1-1963)
4-3-11: PENALTY FOR VIOLATIONS:
Any person who shall violate the provisions of this Code, or neglect or refuse
to comply with any order of notice made by the electrical inspector pursuant to
the provisions of this Code shall be deemed guilty of a misdemeanor and upon
conviction thereof shall be subject to a fine as established in the master fee
schedule. (Ord. 357, 4-1-1963; amd. Ord. 925, 10-1-2018)
CHAPTER 4
FIRE CODE
SECTION:
4-4-1: Adoption Of Fire Code
4-4-1: ADOPTION OF FIRE CODE:
There is hereby adopted, for the purpose of prescribing regulations governing
conditions hazardous to life and property from fire or explosion, the most
current version of the International Fire Code, as adopted by the State of
Idaho, including all appendices thereto, and the same is hereby adopted and
incorporated as though fully set forth at length herein.
The City Clerk shall maintain not less than one duly certified copy of the most
current version of the International Fire Code at the Office of the City Clerk
for use and examination by the public during normal business hours, in
accordance with Idaho Code, section 50-901. (Ord. 917, 1-2-2018)
CHAPTER 5
FLOOD HAZARD REGULATIONS
SECTION:
4-5-1: Authority; Purpose Of Chapter
4-5-1-1: Statutory Authorization
4-5-1-2: Findings Of Fact
4-5-1-3: Statement Of Purpose
4-5-1-4: Methods Of Reducing Flood Losses
4-5-2: Definitions
4-5-3: General Provisions
4-5-3-1: Lands To Which This Chapter Applies
4-5-3-2: Basis For Establishing The Areas Of Special Flood Hazard
4-5-3-3: Compliance
4-5-3-4: Abrogation And Greater Restrictions
4-5-3-5: Interpretation
4-5-3-6: Warning And Disclaimer Of Liability
4-5-4: Administration
4-5-4-1: Establishment Of Development Permit
4-5-4-2: Designation Of The Building Inspector
4-5-4-3: Duties And Responsibilities Of The Building Inspector
4-5-4-4: Variance Procedures
4-5-5: Provisions For Flood Hazard Protection
4-5-5-1: General Standards
4-5-5-2: Specific Standards
4-5-5-3: Floodways
4-5-1: AUTHORITY; PURPOSE OF CHAPTER:
4-5-1-1: STATUTORY AUTHORIZATION:
The legislature of the State of Idaho has, in Idaho Code title 50, delegated
responsibility to local governmental units to adopt regulations designed to
promote the public health, safety and general welfare of its citizenry.
Therefore, the City of Grangeville, Idaho County, Idaho does ordain the
following regulations. (Ord. 565, 10-3-1983; amd. Ord. 954, 12-20-2021)
4-5-1-2: FINDINGS OF FACT:
   A.   The flood hazard areas of the City are subject to periodic inundation
which may result in loss of life and property, health, and safety hazards,
disruption of commerce and governmental services, extraordinary public
expenditures for flood protection and relief, and impairment of the tax base,
all of which adversely affect the public health, safety, and general welfare.
   B.   These flood losses may be caused by the cumulative effect of
obstructions in areas of special flood hazards, which increase flood heights
and velocities, and when inadequately anchored, damage uses in other areas.
Uses that are inadequately floodproofed, elevated or otherwise protected from
flood damage also contribute to the flood loss. (Ord. 565, 10-3-1983; amd. Ord.
954, 12-20-2021)
4-5-1-3: STATEMENT OF PURPOSE:
It is the purpose of this Chapter to promote the public health, safety, and
general welfare, and to minimize public and private losses due to flood
conditions in specific areas by provisions designed:
   A.   To protect human life and health;
   B.   To minimize expenditure of public money and costly flood control
projects;
   C.   To minimize the need for rescue and relief efforts associated with
flooding and generally undertaken at the expense of the general public;
   D.   To minimize prolonged business interruptions;
   E.   To minimize damage to public facilities and utilities such as water and
gas mains, electric, telephone and sewer lines, streets, and bridges located in
areas of special flood hazard;
   F.   To help maintain a stable tax base by providing for the sound use and
development of areas of special flood hazard so as to minimize future flood
blight areas;
   G.   To ensure that potential buyers are notified that property is in an
area of special flood hazard; and
   H.   To ensure that those who occupy the areas of special flood hazard
assume responsibility for their actions. (Ord. 565, 10-3-1983; amd. Ord. 954,
12-20-2021)
4-5-1-4: METHODS OF REDUCING FLOOD LOSSES:
In order to accomplish its purposes, this Chapter includes methods and
provisions for:
   A.   Restricting or prohibiting uses which are dangerous to health, safety,
and property due to water or erosion hazards, or which result in damaging
increases in erosion or in flood heights or velocities;
   B.   Requiring that uses vulnerable to floods, including facilities which
serve such uses, be protected against flood damage at the time of initial
constructions;
   C.   Controlling the alteration of natural floodplains, stream channels, and
natural protective barriers, which help accommodate or channel flood waters;
   D.   Controlling filling, grading, dredging, and other development which may
increase flood damage; and
   E.   Preventing or regulating the construction of flood barriers which will
unnaturally divert flood waters or which may increase flood hazards in other
areas. (Ord. 565, 10-3-1983; amd. Ord. 954, 12-20-2021)
4-5-2: DEFINITIONS:
Unless specifically defined below, words or phrases used in this Chapter shall
be interpreted so as to give them the meaning they have in common usage and to
give this Chapter its most reasonable application.
APPEAL:        A request for a review of the Building Inspector's interpretation of any provision
               of this Chapter or a request for a variance.
AREA OF        A designated AO or AH Zone on the Flood Insurance Rate Map (FIRM). The base flood
SHALLOW        depths range from one foot (1') to three feet (3'); a clearly defined channel does
FLOODING:      not exist; the path of flooding is unpredictable and indeterminate; and, velocity
               flow may be evident.
AREA OF        The land in the floodplain within a community subject to a one percent (1%) chance
SPECIAL FLOOD  of being equaled or exceeded in any given year.
HAZARD:
BASE FLOOD:    The flood having a one percent (1%) chance of being equaled or exceeded in any
               given year.
BASE FLOOD
ELEVATION      The elevation to which floodwater is anticipated to rise during the base flood.
(BFE):
BASEMENT:      Any area of the building having its floor sub-grade, i.e., below ground level, on
               all sides.
BUILDING:      See "STRUCTURE."
               Any manmade change to improved or unimproved real estate, including, but not
DEVELOPMENT:   limited to, buildings or other structures, mining, dredging, filling, grading,
               paving, excavation or drilling operations or storage of equipment or materials
               located within the area of special flood hazard.

SUBDIVISION:   pads, and the construction of streets) is completed before the effective date of
               this Chapter.
EXPANSION TO

PARK OR MOBILE installation of or utilities, either final site grading or pouring of concrete
HOME           pads, or the construction of streets).
SUBDIVISION:
               A general and temporary condition or partial or complete inundation of normally
               dry land areas from:
               A.   The overflow of inland or tidal waters; and/or
               B.   The unusual and rapid accumulation of runoff of surface waters from any
               source.
               C.   Mudslides (i.e., mudflows) which are proximately caused by flooding as
               defined in paragraph B of this definition and are akin to a river of liquid and
FLOOD OR       flowing mud on the surfaces of normally dry land areas, as when earth is carried
FLOODING:      by a current of water and deposited along the path of the current.
               The collapse or subsidence of land along the shore of a lake or other body of
               water as a result of erosion or undermining caused by waves or currents of water
               exceeding anticipated cyclical levels or suddenly caused by an unusually high
               water level in a natural body of water, accompanied by a severe storm, or by an
               unanticipated force of nature, such as flash flood or an abnormal tidal surge, or
               by some similarly unusual and unforeseeable event which results in flooding as
               defined in paragraph A of this definition.
FLOOD          The official map on which the Federal Insurance Administrator has delineated both
INSURANCE RATE the areas of special flood hazards and the risk premium zones applicable to the
MAP (FIRM):    community.

INSURANCE      corresponding water surface elevations, or an examination, evaluation and
STUDY:         determination of mudslide (i.e., mudflow) and/or flood-related erosion hazards
               (also known as Flood Elevation Study).
               Any combination of structural and nonstructural additions, changes, or adjustments
FLOOD          to structures which reduce or eliminate risk of flood damage to real estate or
PROOFING:      improved real property, water and sanitary facilities, structures, and their
               contents.
FLOODPLAIN     The community official designated by title to administer and enforce the
ADMINISTRATOR: floodplain management regulations.
FLOODPLAIN     The operation of an overall program of corrective and preventive measures for
MANAGEMENT:    reducing flood damage, including but not limited to emergency preparedness plans,
               flood control works, and floodplain management regulations.
               Zoning ordinances, subdivision regulations, building codes, health regulations,
FLOODPLAIN     special purpose ordinances (such as floodplain ordinance, grading ordinance and
MANAGEMENT     erosion control ordinance) and other application of police power. The term
REGULATIONS:   describes such state or local regulations, in any combination thereof, which
               provide standards for the purpose of flood damage prevention and reduction.
FLOODPLAIN OR  Any land area susceptible to being inundated by water from any source. See "FLOOD
FLOOD PRONE    or FLOODING."
AREA:
               The channel of a river or other watercourse and the adjacent land areas that must
FLOODWAY:      be reserved in order to discharge the base flood without cumulatively increasing
               the water surface elevation more than a designated height.
               A use which cannot perform its intended purpose unless it is located or carried
FUNCTIONALLY   out in close proximity to water. The term includes only docking facilities, port
DEPENDENT USE: facilities that are necessary for the loading and unloading of cargo or

HIGHEST        The highest natural elevation of the ground surface prior to construction next to
ADJACENT       the proposed walls of a structure.

               Any structure that is:

                  b.   Directly by the Secretary of the Interior in states without approved

               The lowest floor of the lowest enclosed area (including basement). An unfinished
               or flood resistant enclosure, usable solely for parking of vehicles, building
LOWEST FLOOR:  access or storage in an area other than a basement area is not considered a
               building's lowest floor, provided that such enclosure is not built so as to render
               the structure in violation of the applicable non-elevation design requirements of

               A structure, transportable in one or more sections, which is built on a permanent
MANUFACTURED   chassis and is designed for use with or without a permanent foundation when
HOME:          attached to the required utilities. The term "manufactured home" does not include
               a "recreational vehicle."
MANUFACTURED   A parcel (or contiguous parcels) of land divided into two (2) or more manufactured
HOME PARK OR   home lots for rent or sale.
SUBDIVISION:

               Section
MOBILE HOME:   10-2-1. Mobile homes shall include, for purposes of this Chapter, those produced

               10-2-1.

NEW            any subsequent improvements to such structures. For floodplain management
CONSTRUCTION:  purposes, "new construction" means structures for which the "start of
               construction" commenced on or after the effective date of a floodplain management

               structures.
NEW MOBILE     A parcel (or contiguous parcels) of land divided into two (2) or more mobile home
HOME PARK OR   lots for rent or sale for which the construction of facilities for servicing the
MOBILE HOME    lot (including, at a minimum the installation of utilities, either final site
SUBDIVISION:   grading or the pouring of concrete pads, and the construction of streets) is

VEHICLE:       3.    Designed to be self propelled or permanently towable by a light duty truck;
               and
               4.   Designed primarily not for use as a permanent dwelling but as temporary
               living quarters for recreational, camping, travel, or seasonal use.
               Includes substantial improvement and means the date the building permit as issued,
               provided the actual start of construction, repair, reconstruction, rehabilitation,
               addition, placement, or other improvement was within one hundred eighty (180) days
               from the date of the permit. The actual start means either the first placement of
               permanent construction of a structure on a site, such as the pouring of slab or
               footings, the installation of piles, the construction of columns, or any work
               beyond the stage of excavation; or the placement of a manufactured home on a
START OF       foundation. Permanent construction does not include land preparation, such as
CONSTRUCTION:  clearing, grading, and filling; nor does it include the installation of streets

               wall, ceiling, floor, or other structural part of a building, whether or not that
               alteration affects the external dimensions of the building.
STRUCTURE:     A walled and roofed building including a gas or liquid storage tank, that is

SUBSTANTIAL    Damage of any origin sustained by a structure whereby the cost of restoring the
DAMAGE:        structure to its before damaged condition would equal or exceed fifty percent
               (50%) of the market value of the structure before the damage occurred.

               structure before the "start of construction" of the improvement. This term
               includes structures which have incurred "substantial damage," regardless of the
               actual repair work performed.
SUBSTANTIAL    The term does not, however, include either:
IMPROVEMENT:   A.   Any project for improvement of a structure to correct existing violations of
