o'clock (7:00) A.M. of any day. Violators of this provision may have their
license revoked at the discretion of the City Council. (Ord. 621, 12-18-1989)
5-6A-7: REGULATIONS:
It shall be unlawful for any person to offer beer to any person under the age
of twenty one (21) years and it shall be unlawful for any person under the age
of twenty one (21) years to frequent, loiter in or about or patronize any beer
dispensary and it shall likewise be unlawful for any owner of such beer
dispensary or his employees to permit any such person under the age of twenty
one (21) years to be in or to be employed in such dispensary. (Ord. 621, 12-18-
1989)
5-6A-8: REVOCATION:
The Governing Body shall retain the right at all times to revoke and cancel any
license for just cause. When any license is revoked the licensee shall have the
privilege of appearing before the Governing Body to appeal such revocation. Any
conduct or act on the part of the licensee which may be sufficient cause for
revocation of the license must be brought to the attention of the City Council.
(1959 Code)
5-6A-9: LICENSE TRANSFER:
Any license issued hereunder shall be transferable under the same terms and
conditions which govern the transfer of beer licenses issued by the State of
Idaho, as set forth in Idaho Code, title 23, chapter 10, and which are
incorporated herein by reference as completely as though expressly set forth as
those terms and provisions may be made applicable to Municipal license
transfer. The fee as established in the master fee schedule shall be payable to
the City Clerk upon any such application for transfer being filed with such
office, and shall constitute the entire fee imposed by the City for such
transfer. (Ord. 645, 10-5-1992; amd. Ord. 925, 10-1-2018)
5-6A-10: PENALTY:
Any person who violates any of the provisions of this chapter and article or
fails to comply with any of the terms and conditions of this Act shall be
guilty of a misdemeanor. (Ord. 743, 11-19-2001)
CHAPTER 6
LIQUOR CONTROL
ARTICLE B. LIQUOR BY THE DRINK
SECTION:
5-6B-1: Licensed Liquor Sale
5-6B-2: Application
5-6B-3: Requirements
5-6B-4: Fees
5-6B-5: License Transfer
5-6B-6: Licenses Limited
5-6B-7: Revocation And Hearing
5-6B-8: Access To Premises
5-6B-9: Premises Requirements
5-6B-10: Sale To Minors Prohibited
5-6B-11: Processing Of Applications
5-6B-12: Hours Of Sale
5-6B-13: Penalty
5-6B-1: LICENSED LIQUOR SALE:
It shall be unlawful to sell liquor by the drink as provided in Idaho Code,
title 23, chapter 9, and wine by the drink on Sunday, provided a license shall
be obtained as provided in this article and the rules and regulations and
provisions concerning the licensing and operation of a place of business for
the sale of liquor as above allowed, and wine on Sunday are adhered to as
provided. (Ord. 550, 12-7-1981)
5-6B-2: APPLICATION:
Before there shall be any lawful sale of liquor by the drink an application by
the proposed licensee must be made for such license and filed with the City
Clerk in form and manner herein provided. Such application shall provide for
the name of the applicant, the location of the proposed business, and such
other information as may be prescribed and required by the City Council. At the
time said application is filed the applicant shall also present a copy of an
application for a State license and also the license issued by the State for
the sale of liquor by the drink at retail and no license will be issued until a
license is first obtained from the State.
All applications filed with the City Clerk shall be referred to the City
Council for final approval. The City Clerk shall receive the license fee
hereinafter provided at the time of filing of the application and upon approval
of the application by the City Council the license will be issued and delivered
to the applicant. (1959 Code)
5-6B-3: REQUIREMENTS:
No license shall be issued for the sale of liquor by the drink to any person
not qualified for a license under Idaho Code, title 23, chapter 9, nor upon any
premises in any neighborhood which is predominately residential nor within
three hundred feet (300') of any school, church or other places of public
worship. (1959 Code)
5-6B-4: FEES:
   A.   The license fee required of an applicant for the sale of liquor by the
drink and wine by the drink on Sunday, included therein shall be as established
in the master fee schedule payable in advance. The first payment shall be made
with the application for the balance of the fiscal year in which the license is
issued. All licenses issued to be effective after February 1, 2003, shall
expire on January 31 of the year following their issuance. Renewals may be
granted upon such application, if the record of the applicant is satisfactory
to the City Council in accordance with the provisions of the law and this
article and upon payment of a fee as established in the master fee schedule.
Any operation under an expired license shall constitute a violation of this
Code for each day of operation. (Ord. 743, 11-19-2001; amd. Ord. 925, 10-1-
2018)
5-6B-5: LICENSE TRANSFER:
Any license issued hereunder shall be transferable under the same terms and
conditions which govern the transfer of liquor by the drink licenses issued by
the State of Idaho, as set forth in Idaho Code, title 23, chapter 9, and which
are incorporated herein by this reference as completely and expressly set forth
as those terms and provisions may be made applicable to Municipal license
transfers. A fee as established in the master fee schedule shall be payable to
the City Clerk upon any such application for transfer being filed with such
office, and shall constitute the entire fee imposed by the City for such
transfer. (Ord. 646, 10-5-1992; amd. Ord. 925, 10-1-2018)
5-6B-6: LICENSES LIMITED:
The number of liquor licenses issued and operative may be limited in number by
action of the City Council. (1959 Code)
5-6B-7: REVOCATION AND HEARING:
If any licensee or employee of a liquor by the drink establishment violates any
of the provisions of this article or is convicted of the violation of any of
the provisions of Idaho Code, title 23, chapter 9, the City Council is hereby
authorized and empowered to revoke the license issued to said licensee;
provided, however, that in the event it is brought to the attention of the City
Council that a violation has taken place, before revoking such license, the
City Council shall cause notice to be served upon the licensee, setting forth
in general terms the violation or violations claimed to have been committed and
such notice shall provide a time for hearing thereon by the City Council which
date of hearing shall not be less than five (5) days nor more than ten (10)
days from the date of the service of said notice, and upon or following said
hearing the City Council, if they shall find that the provisions of this
article or the provisions of the laws of the State have been violated shall
revoke such license theretofore issued and no refund of any unused portion of
the license fee shall be made to the licensee. A revocation by the Commission
of Law Enforcement of the State of any license theretofore issued said licensee
shall automatically revoke the license issued by the City and no refund of any
fee therefore paid shall be made. (1959 Code)
5-6B-8: ACCESS TO PREMISES:
All peace officers appointed by the State or the City or the County shall have
free access at all times to the licensed premises, and any information touching
the manner and method of the operation of said premises or the sale of said
liquor may be submitted to the Governing Body upon any investigation made of
said licensee. (1959 Code)
5-6B-9: PREMISES REQUIREMENTS:
Every licensee must conform to all regulations and laws of the State and the
provisions of this article. Liquor by the drink shall not be sold by any person
except one duly licensed. Full and unobstructed view of the inside of the
premises where said liquor by the drink is sold shall always be maintained by
said licensee and no obstructions whatever shall be placed upon the windows or
the doors that are located on said premises and no coloring shall be placed
upon the glass in order that a full view from the sidewalk or street may be had
into the interior of said premises. All premises shall be adequately lighted
and subject to periodic sanitary inspection. No gambling devices shall be
maintained thereon. Every licensed establishment shall maintain and have a
window opening to permit police officers a view inside of such establishment
after the hours of closing. (1959 Code)
5-6B-10: SALE TO MINORS PROHIBITED:
No sale of liquor shall be made to any minor nor to any intoxicated person who
may engage in disorderly or improper conduct and no disorderly or improper
entertainment shall be permitted upon said premises and any violation of the
provisions of this article shall be considered and shall likewise be grounds
for the cancellation of the license. (1959 Code)
5-6B-11: PROCESSING OF APPLICATIONS:
In addition to the revocation and hearing provisions set forth in this article,
the receipt of an application for permission to sell liquor by the drink shall
be handled in accordance with those provisions in article A of this chapter
relating to beer license applications except where the same may be in conflict
with the previous provisions of this article or State law. (Ord. 569, 12-19-
1983)
5-6B-12: HOURS OF SALE:
   A.   Adoption Of Regulations: This article is adopted pursuant to the
authority conferred by Idaho Code 23-927, 23-1012 and 23-1332 and Idaho County
ordinance 30, adopted by the Idaho County Commissioners on August 28, 1987,
which statutes and County ordinance provide that the County and City may, by
ordinance, allow the sale of liquor by the drink on Sundays, Memorial Day,
Thanksgiving and may also extend until two o'clock (2:00) A.M. the hours of
sale of liquor by the drink, beer and wine.
   B.   Sunday Sales: Liquor by the drink may be sold, offered for sale or
given away on any licensed premises under the same rules, limitations and
conditions as applied to all of the days of the week. (Ord. 605, 9-8-1987)
   C.   Hours Of Sale Of Liquor By The Drink: No liquor by the drink shall be
sold, offered for sale or given away upon any licensed premises and all liquor
not in sealed bottles must be locked in a separate room or cabinet during the
following hours:
      1.   Christmas from the hour of two o'clock (2:00) A.M. to the hour of
ten o'clock (10:00) A.M. the following day.
      2.   On any other day between the hour of two o'clock (2:00) A.M. and the
hour of ten o'clock (10:00) A.M. (Ord. 879, 10-15-2012)
   D.   Time Allowed For Closing: Any patron present on any licensed premises
after the sale of liquor by the drink, wine and beer has stopped as provided in
subsection C of this section and section
5-6A-6 of this chapter shall have a reasonable time not to exceed thirty (30)
minutes to consume any beverages already served.
   E.   Additional Duties:
      1.   Any person who consumes or intentionally permits the consumption of
any alcoholic beverage upon licensed premises during any closed periods
provided in this section shall be guilty of a misdemeanor as defined in Idaho
Code 18-111 and 18-113.
      2.   It shall be the duty of every person who is employed at or upon any
licensed premises or who owns or manages a licensed premises and who is present
upon the licensed premises during the hours and the times set forth in this
section concerning liquor by the drink, to lock up and keep locked up in a
locked room or locked cabinet all unsealed containers of liquor, and any such
person who fails to perform the duty provided herein shall be guilty of a
misdemeanor as provided in Idaho Code 18-111 and 18-113. (Ord. 605, 9-8-1987)
5-6B-13: PENALTY:
Any person who violates the terms and provisions of this chapter and article or
fails to comply with the terms and provisions of this Act shall be guilty of a
misdemeanor. (Ord. 743, 11-19-2001)
CHAPTER 6
LIQUOR CONTROL
ARTICLE C. WINE
SECTION:
5-6C-1: Definitions
5-6C-2: License Required
5-6C-3: Application For License
5-6C-4: Qualifications
5-6C-5: License Fee
5-6C-6: Issuance Of License
5-6C-7: License Restrictions
5-6C-8: Consumption On Premises
5-6C-9: Possession
5-6C-10: Misrepresentation Of Age
5-6C-11: Revocation Of License
5-6C-12: Penalty
5-6C-13: Severability
5-6C-1: DEFINITIONS:
The following terms as used in this Act are hereby defined as follows:
COMMISSIONER: The Commissioner of Law Enforcement of the State of Idaho.
PERSON: Includes an individual, firm, copartnership, association, corporation,
or any group or combination acting as a unit, and includes the plural as well
as the singular unless the intent to give a more limited meaning is disclosed
by the context in which it is used.
RETAIL WINE LICENSE: A license issued by the Commissioner, authorizing a person
to sell wine at retail.
RETAILER: A person to whom a retail wine license has been issued.
WINE: Any alcoholic beverage containing not more than fourteen percent (14%)
alcohol by volume obtained by the fermentation of the natural sugar content of
fruits or other agricultural products containing sugar. (Ord. 420, 7-8-1971)
5-6C-2: LICENSE REQUIRED:
It shall be lawful for any person to sell wine at retail within the corporate
limits of the City after having first procured a license therefor. (Ord. 420,
7-8-1971)
5-6C-3: APPLICATION FOR LICENSE:
An application for a wine license under this article or under article D of this
chapter shall be processed and administered in the same way as a beer license
is processed and administered pursuant to section
5-6A-3 of this chapter, subject to any peculiar regulations relating to wine
that may appear from time to time in the Idaho Code. (Ord. 568, 12-19-1983)
5-6C-4: QUALIFICATIONS:
The applicant for a license shall possess all of the qualifications necessary
to obtain a license from the Commissioner of Law Enforcement of the State, as
prescribed by the laws of the State, and maintain such qualifications
throughout the period for which such license is issued. The possession of
licenses regularly issued by the Department of Law Enforcement and the County
in addition to a City beer license, shall be prima facie evidence of the
applicant's qualifications to receive a license hereunder. (Ord. 420, 7-8-1971)
5-6C-5: LICENSE FEE:
   A.   The license fee imposed and collected shall be as established in the
master fee schedule. Such license shall begin for the period of time commencing
February 1, 2003 through January 31 of the following year; provided, however,
should a license be issued for less than a full fiscal year the license fee
shall be prorated in accordance with the actual months of issuance. (Ord. 743,
11-19-2001; amd. Ord. 925, 10-1-2018)
5-6C-6: ISSUANCE OF LICENSE:
Upon filing the application for a license and production of evidence as
required by section
5-6C-4 of this article as to the qualifications of the applicant and by the
payment of the required license fee, the City Clerk shall upon approval of the
City Council, issue to the applicant a license to sell wine at retail within
the Municipality for such calendar year or the remainder thereof. (Ord. 420, 7-
8-1971)
5-6C-7: LICENSE RESTRICTIONS:
The assignment or transfer of a wine license shall be the same as provided by
section
5-6A-9 of this chapter for the assignment or transfer of a beer license. (Ord.
420, 7-8-1971)
5-6C-8: CONSUMPTION ON PREMISES:
Retailers who do not possess a valid license for the retail sale of liquor by
the drink shall not permit consumption of wine on the licensed premises and may
sell the wine only in its original unbroken, sealed container. Wine sold for
consumption on the retailer's premises may be sold only during hours that
liquor by the drink may be sold pursuant to the laws of this State. Wine sold
by the retailer for consumption off the premises of the retailer may be sold
only during the hours that beer may be sold pursuant to the laws of this State.
(Ord. 420, 7-8-1971)
5-6C-9: POSSESSION:
No person may, while operating or riding in or upon a motor vehicle upon a
public highway of this State, have in his possession any wine in an open or
unsealed container of any kind. (Ord. 420, 7-8-1971)
5-6C-10: MISREPRESENTATION OF AGE:
   A.   No person under the age of twenty one (21) years may purchase, consume
or possess wine.
   B.   No person shall give, sell, or deliver wine to any person under the age
of twenty one (21) years.
   C.   No person under the age of twenty one (21) years shall by any means
represent to any retailer or distributor or to any agent or employee of such
retailer or distributor that he or she is twenty one (21) years or more of age
for the purpose of inducing such retailer or distributor, or his agent or
employee, to sell, service or dispense wine to such person.
   D.   No person shall, by any means, represent to any retailer or distributor
or agent or employee of such retailer or distributor, that any other person is
twenty one (21) years or more of age, when in fact such other person is under
the age of twenty one (21) years, for the purpose of inducing such retailer or
distributor, or the agent or employee of such retailer or distributor, to sell,
serve, or dispense wine to such other person. (Ord. 420, 7-8-1971)
5-6C-11: REVOCATION OF LICENSE:
The right shall be and remain at all times vested in the Mayor and City
Council, and the Mayor and City Council may, as hereinafter provided, revoke or
cancel any license for fraud or misrepresentation in its procurement, or for a
violation of any of the provisions of this article, or for any conduct or act
of the licensee or his employees or any conduct or act permitted by him or them
on the premises where such business is conducted, or in connection therewith or
adjacent thereto, tending to render such business or such premises where the
same is conducted as a public nuisance or a menace to the health, peace, safety
or general welfare of the City; provided, that revocation or suspension of the
State license by the Commissioner of Law Enforcement shall be deemed prima
facie evidence for revocation or suspension of the license issued herein. (Ord.
420, 7-8-1971)
5-6C-12: PENALTY:
Any person who violates any of the provisions of this Act or fails to comply
with any of the terms and conditions of this Act shall be guilty of a
misdemeanor. (Ord. 420, 7-8-1971)
5-6C-13: SEVERABILITY:
The provisions of this Act are hereby declared to be severable and if any
provision of this Act or the application of such provision to any person or
circumstance is declared invalid for any reason, such declaration shall not
affect the validity of the remaining portions of this Act. (Ord. 420, 7-8-1971)
CHAPTER 6
LIQUOR CONTROL
ARTICLE D. WINE BY THE DRINK
SECTION:
5-6D-1: License Required
5-6D-2: Application For License
5-6D-3: Qualifications
5-6D-4: License Fee
5-6D-5: Issuance Of License
5-6D-6: License Restrictions
5-6D-7: Penalty
5-6D-8: Severability
5-6D-9: License Transfer
5-6D-1: LICENSE REQUIRED:
In accordance with the provisions of chapter 144 of the Idaho Session Laws of
the first regular session of the Forty Second Legislature, and upon the
provisions of Idaho Code 23-1315, it shall be lawful to any person to sell wine
at retail, by the drink, within the corporate limits of the City, after having
first procured a license therefor. (Ord. 438, 6-11-1973)
5-6D-2: APPLICATION FOR LICENSE:
Application for license shall be in writing, signed and sworn to by the
applicant and upon application forms furnished by the City Clerk. Such
application shall be filed by the City Clerk and presented to the Mayor and
City Council at the next scheduled meeting of the City Council for their
approval, rejection or further consideration. (Ord. 438, 6-11-1973)
5-6D-3: QUALIFICATIONS:
The applicant for a license shall possess all of the qualifications necessary
to obtain a license from the Commissioner of Law Enforcement of the State, as
prescribed by the laws of the State, and maintain such qualifications
throughout the period for which such license is issued. The possession of
licenses regularly issued by the Department of Law Enforcement and the County
in addition to a City beer license, shall be prima facie evidence of the
applicant's qualifications to receive a license hereunder. A licensee for
liquor by the drink shall not be required to obtain an additional license under
the provisions of this article. (Ord. 438, 6-11-1973)
5-6D-4: LICENSE FEE:
   A.   The license fee imposed and collected shall be as established in the
master fee schedule. Such license year shall be from February 1, 2003 through
January 31 of the following year; provided, however, should a license be issued
for less than a full fiscal year, the license fee shall be prorated in
accordance with the actual months of issuance. (Ord. 743, 11-19-2001; amd. Ord.
925, 10-1-2018)
5-6D-5: ISSUANCE OF LICENSE:
Upon filing the application for a license and production of evidence as
required by this article, as to the qualifications of the applicant, and by the
payment of the required license fee, the City Clerk shall upon approval of the
City Council, issue to the applicant a license to sell wine at retail, by the
drink, within the City for such calendar year or remainder thereof. (Ord. 438,
6-11-1973)
5-6D-6: LICENSE RESTRICTIONS:
The assignment or transfer of wine by the drink license, issued hereunder,
shall be the same as provided for the assignment or transfer of beer license.
(Ord. 438, 6-11-1973)
5-6D-7: PENALTY:
Any person who violates any of the provisions of this article or fails to
comply with any of the terms and conditions hereof, shall be guilty of a
misdemeanor and be punished for such violation by a fine as established in the
master fee schedule or jail sentence up to thirty (30) days, or by both such
fine and sentence. (Ord. 438, 6-11-1973; amd. Ord. 925, 10-1-2018)
5-6D-8: SEVERABILITY:
The provisions of this Act are hereby declared to be severable and if any
provision of this Act or the application of such provision to any person or
circumstance is declared invalid for any reason, such declaration shall not
affect the validity of the remaining portions of this Act. (Ord. 438, 6-11-
1973)
5-6D-9: LICENSE TRANSFER:
Any license which relates to the sale of wine either by the drink or by
package, if not included in a liquor license, shall be transferable under the
same terms and conditions which govern the transfer of wine licenses issued by
the State of Idaho, as set forth in Idaho Code, title 23, chapter 13, and which
are incorporated herein by this reference as completely and expressly set forth
as those terms and provisions may be made applicable to Municipal license
transfer. A fee as established in the master fee schedule shall be payable to
the City Clerk upon any application for transfer being filed with such office
and shall constitute the entire fee imposed by the City for such transfer.
(Ord. 647, 10-5-1992; amd. Ord. 925, 10-1-2018)
CHAPTER 7
PRIVATE SECURITY SERVICES
SECTION:
5-7-1: Definitions
5-7-2: License Required
5-7-3: Application For License
5-7-4: Standards For Issuance Of License
5-7-5: License Fee
5-7-6: Action By Council; Notice Of Rejection
5-7-7: Licenses Nontransferable
5-7-8: Revocation And Suspension Of Licenses
5-7-9: Renewal Of Licenses
5-7-10: Term Of Licensing
5-7-11: Bond Requirements
5-7-12: Investigation By Chief Of Police
5-7-13: Fingerprints And Photographs
5-7-14: Regulations
5-7-15: Posting And Carrying Of Licenses
5-7-16: Impersonation Of Officers
5-7-17: Requirements For Employees
5-7-18: Save Harmless Agreement
5-7-1: DEFINITIONS:
For the purposes of this Chapter, the following words and phrases shall have
the meanings indicated unless context clearly requires otherwise:
PRIVATE SECURITY OFFICER OR SERVICE: Any person or corporation who accepts
employment for hire, fee, or reward to protect private property during the
nighttime or at any other time, to furnish protection to private property
during the nighttime or any other time, to furnish protection to private
property by checking the doors, windows, and other exits of private property
located within the City or to furnish any other services incidental to and in
connection with the protection of private property within the City, except
those persons hired directly as night watchmen by individual businesses and
whose full time duties consist of keeping watch over a single store or single
place of business. (Ord. 579, 4-1-1985)
5-7-2: LICENSE REQUIRED:
No person shall operate a private security service in this City without first
having obtained a license from the City as provided herein. (Ord. 579, 4-1-
1985)
5-7-3: APPLICATION FOR LICENSE:
Applications for licenses as required by this Chapter shall be made upon blank
forms prepared and made available by the Chief of Police and shall state at a
minimum, the following:
   A.   The full name, other names used, age, residence, present occupation of
the applicant, and occupations for ten (10) years previous to the date of
application.
   B.   Whether the person signing the application is a citizen of the United
States.
   C.   A specific description of the location of the principal place of
business of the applicant and the location of offices used by the applicant.
   D.   Previous experience, if any, that the applicant has had as a private
security officer, law enforcement officer, or experience in other related
fields.
   E.   The length of time that the applicant has been a bona fide resident of
the State, immediately preceding the filing of the application and information
concerning residence for a five (5) year period of time preceding the
application.
   F.   Whether the applicant, or any person that would be an employee of the
applicant has any criminal record whatsoever.
   G.   Whether the applicant or persons actually engaging in the work are
certified in the State for the care and handling of firearms. (Ord. 579, 4-1-
1985)
5-7-4: STANDARDS FOR ISSUANCE OF LICENSE:
The City Council shall issue a license as required by this chapter when it is
found:
   A.   That the applicant is a citizen of the United States.
   B.   That the applicant, if an individual, or its principals, if a business
association, are of good moral character.
   C.   That the applicant, if an individual, or its principals, if a business
association, have not been convicted of a felony or any crime of moral
turpitude in this State or any other state in the ten (10) years previous to
the date of the application and such person or persons are not on parole or
probation for any offense whatsoever. It shall be a further requirement that
any applicant or principal of any business association, shall not have had a
felony sentence, parole or probation that was terminated within the five (5)
years previous to the date of the application.
   D.   If the application or subsequent investigation reflects a felony
conviction of any applicant or principal in any business association occurring
at any time, then that person shall have additionally lived within Idaho
County, Idaho for at least one year prior to the date of the application. (Ord.
579, 4-1-1985)
5-7-5: LICENSE FEE:
The annual license fee for a person acting as a private security officer on
services shall be as established in the master fee schedule. (Ord. 579, 4-1-
1985; amd. Ord. 925, 10-1-2018)
5-7-6: ACTION BY COUNCIL; NOTICE OF REJECTION:
   A.   The City Council shall act upon the application for a private security
service within thirty (30) days after the filing of the application with the
City Clerk. If the City Council disapproves the application, there shall be
mailed to the applicant, within thirty (30) days after the date upon which the
application was filed, a notice of the City Council stating the reasons for the
denial of the permit. Thereafter, within fifteen (15) days, the applicant may
request a hearing before the City Council for a review of the application and
all relevant information shall be submitted at the hearing.
   B.   In the event the permit shall be denied after hearing, the applicant
shall have the right to appeal to the District Court in and for Idaho County,
Idaho within thirty (30) days after the final denial is received by the
applicant. The standard for review in the District Court shall be based upon an
abuse of discretion by the City Council in denying the permit. (Ord. 579, 4-1-
1985)
5-7-7: LICENSE NONTRANSFERABLE:
Licenses under this chapter shall not be transferrable. (Ord. 579, 4-1-1985)
5-7-8: REVOCATION AND SUSPENSION OF LICENSES:
Licenses issued under this chapter shall be subject to revocation or suspension
by the City Council for violation of any of the provisions of this chapter or
misconduct by the licensee or his employees, after reasonable notice and
opportunity to be heard has been given the licensee. The Chief of Police shall
immediately notify any licensee by personal service of such suspension or
revocation. The hearing shall be conducted in accordance with the hearing
procedures adopted previously by Grangeville resolution 73. (Ord. 579, 4-1-
1985)
5-7-9: RENEWAL OF LICENSES:
The City Council shall renew licenses to any licensee whose license has not
been suspended at the time such licenses have expired, upon payment of the
annual license fee. (Ord. 579, 4-1-1985)
5-7-10: TERM OF LICENSING:
All licenses issued under this chapter shall be for a term of one year and run
from the date of issuance one year forward. (Ord. 579, 4-1-1985)
5-7-11: BOND REQUIREMENTS:
No license shall be issued under this chapter unless the applicant files with
the City a surety bond executed by the applicant with two (2) or more sureties
pursuant to Idaho law relating to undertakings, by a surety company authorized
to do business in this State, or by the posting of a cash bond, with any such
bonds being equal to the sum of fifteen thousand dollars ($15,000.00) provided
that such security is previously approved by the City Attorney with all
bondings being conditioned upon careful, faithful and honest conduct of the
services to be performed by the applicant or his employees. City Attorney
approval shall be as to the form, execution and sufficiency of sureties in each
case.
Such bond as approved security or securities shall be taken in the name of the
City for the benefit of its residents. Each person injured by the negligent,
wilful, malicious or wrongful act of the licensee, his agent, servant or
employee, in the conduct of the business of a private security officer or
business may bring an action on such bond in his own name, to recover damages
for such negligent, wilful, malicious or wrongful act.
Any license shall be subject to suspension by the City Council when the bond or
other approved financial security as required by this section shall have lapsed
or is reduced by reason of a judgment thereon or for any other reason is no
longer in force and effect, after reasonable notice and an opportunity to
reinstate such financial security has been given, such notice being a seventy
two (72) hour minimum. (Ord. 579, 4-1-1985)
5-7-12: INVESTIGATION BY CHIEF OF POLICE:
After a receipt of application for a license as is required by this chapter,
the Chief of Police shall cause an investigation to be made of the applicant
and his proposed operation. The result of such investigation shall be presented
to the City Council as soon as such investigation is completed by the Chief of
Police. Should more than the thirty (30) days as is indicated in section
5-7-6 of this chapter be required for the investigation, the Chief of Police
shall notify the Mayor and the applicant, and the Mayor shall reset the matter
on the grounds within fifteen (15) days of the receipt of the notification, for
the purpose of issuing a temporary restricted license until receipt of the full
investigation. (Ord. 579, 4-1-1985)
5-7-13: FINGERPRINTS AND PHOTOGRAPHS:
The application shall be accompanied by a full set of fingerprints and recent
photographs of the applicant. Furthermore, should the applicant have employees
actively working as security officers, the applicant, if licensed, shall submit
fingerprints and photographs of all such employees to the Chief of Police as a
condition of continued licensing. (Ord. 579, 4-1-1985)
5-7-14: REGULATIONS:
The City Council shall have the authority to enact and enforce reasonable rules
and regulations for the operation of private security personnel. Such
regulations shall be effective upon amendment of this section. Current
regulations are as follows:
   A.   All employees actively engaged as a private security officer shall have
successfully completed a course of firearms handling by an Idaho State
certified instructor, if he is to be in possession of a firearm at any time
during the performance of his duties.
   B.   All employees using a concealed firearm shall be licensed by the County
of Idaho with a permit for the carrying of concealed weapons.
   C.   All employees in possession of a firearm will have a valid Idaho
hunting license. (Ord. 579, 4-1-1985)
5-7-15: POSTING AND CARRYING OF LICENSES:
Any licensee under this chapter shall have a certificate of such license to be
displayed at all times in a conspicuous place in or on his place of business
described in the license. The licensee and all his employees shall carry on
their person at all times when performing services as private security
officers, certified copies of the license as issued under this chapter. (Ord.
579, 4-1-1985)
5-7-16: IMPERSONATION OF OFFICERS:
   A.   No person licensed under this chapter or any employee of licensee shall
impersonate or hold himself out to be a peace officer of this State, nor shall
he operate or permit to be operated a motor vehicle with a siren, blinker
light, or any insignia thereon bearing a likeness to the insignia used by peace
officers of this State.
   B.   No insignia used by any private security officer shall include the word
police at any place within the insignia. (Ord. 579, 4-1-1985)
5-7-17: REQUIREMENTS FOR EMPLOYEES:
   A.   All persons to be hired by licensee as private security officers for a
period of time not to exceed five (5) days shall have provided to the Chief of
Police their fingerprints, photograph, and proper identification, for the
purpose of NCIC investigation, and will not be permitted the carrying or use of
firearms.
   B.   All persons to be hired by licensee as private security officers for a
period of time in excess of five (5) days shall complete an application similar
to that required in section
5-7-3 of this chapter along with fingerprints and photograph, which will be
recorded with the Chief of Police. The Chief of Police may, at his discretion,
cause an investigation to be opened, and may make recommendations to the
licensee as to the character and favorability of the applicant. Provided the
applicant meets the standards as set forth in subsection C1 of this Section,
the acceptability of applicant lies at the discretion of the licensee.
   C.   Standards to be met by applicants:
      1.   All applicants will be citizens of the United States.
      2.   All applicants will be in possession of a valid Idaho driver's
license.
      3.   Applicant has not been convicted of a driving while intoxicated
offense or vehicular homicide offense within the year preceding application.
      4.   Applicant has not been convicted of any felony of this State or any
other state in the ten (10) years previous to this date of application and is
not on parole or probation for any reason at the time of the application.
Additionally, if the application or the subsequent investigation reflects any
felony record of the applicant, then additionally the applicant shall have
lived within Idaho County, Idaho, for a one year period immediately preceding
the date of the application.
      5.   Applicant must be of good moral character.
   D.   The applicant will be issued by licensee, upon hiring, a certificate
stating his name, address, age, social security number, position of employment,
address of employer, his status regarding firearms possession, and whether his
employment is of a temporary (5 days or less) or a permanent nature. (Ord. 579,
4-1-1985)
5-7-18: SAVE HARMLESS AGREEMENT:
A save harmless agreement will be filed with the City upon the approval of
license, in order to release the City from responsibility for the actions of
the licensee or any of his employees. (Ord. 579, 4-1-1985)
CHAPTER 8
TAXICABS
SECTION:
5-8-1: Definitions
5-8-2: License Required; Fee
5-8-3: Applicability Of Chapter
5-8-4: Vehicles - License, Inspection And Insurance Required
5-8-5: Rates To Be Posted
5-8-6: Insignia
5-8-7: Receipt And Discharge Of Passengers
5-8-8: Seating Capacity
5-8-9: State Operator's License Required
5-8-10: Display Of Operator's License
5-8-1: DEFINITIONS:
When used in this chapter the following words shall have the meanings
indicated:
STATE OPERATOR'S LICENSE: The class of operator's license required by the State
of Idaho for the operation of taxicabs or other vehicles for hire.
TAXICABS AND VEHICLES FOR HIRE: Any motor vehicle regularly engaged in the
business of carrying passengers for hire, having a seating capacity of not more
than seven (7) people. (Ord. 706, 10-20-1997)
5-8-2: LICENSE REQUIRED; FEE:
Any person, corporation, partnership or other business entity operating
vehicles required to be licensed under this chapter shall not pay a license fee
for taxi licensing. (Ord. 706, 10-20-1997)
5-8-3: APPLICABILITY OF CHAPTER:
Nothing contained herein shall be construed as applying to the operation of
courtesy automobiles at the Grangeville, Idaho County, Idaho, Airport, but
shall only apply to taxis operated within the City. (Ord. 706, 10-20-1997)
5-8-4: VEHICLES - LICENSE, INSPECTION AND INSURANCE REQUIRED:
   A.   Compliance With Standards: Prior to the use and operation of any
vehicles under the provisions of this chapter, such vehicles shall be
thoroughly examined and inspected by the City police and found to comply with
standards adopted in accordance with the Idaho Driver Education Law Enforcement
Vehicle Inspection Procedures on file with the City police.
   B.   Issuance Of License: When the City finds that a vehicle has met the
standards established by the Chief of Police, the City shall issue a license
for each vehicle complying with the rules and regulations.
   C.   Liability Insurance: In addition, each vehicle licensed hereunder shall
be insured for liability in an amount not less than three hundred thousand
dollars ($300,000.00). Proof of such insurance shall be required prior to
licensing and shall be kept current at all times during the duration of the
license.
   D.   Periodic Inspection: Every vehicle operating under this chapter shall
be annually inspected by the City or at such intervals as shall be established
by the Chief of Police to ensure the continued maintenance of safe operating
conditions. (Ord. 706, 10-20-1997)
   E.   Inspection Fee: The owner of each vehicle inspected under the
provisions of this chapter shall pay a fee to the City as established in the
master fee schedule. (Ord. 706, 10-20-1997; amd. Ord. 925, 10-1-2018)
5-8-5: RATES TO BE POSTED:
Every vehicle licensed hereunder shall clearly post rates for all fares for the
use of the vehicle. Rates shall be posted in such a manner so as to be legible
by all passengers in the vehicle. (Ord. 706, 10-20-1997)
5-8-6: INSIGNIA:
Each vehicle licensed hereunder shall bear on each side, in painted letters,
not less than two inches (2") nor more than four inches (4") in height, the
name of the owner, and it may bear an identifying design. Each vehicle shall
also have an identifying insignia. Each vehicle shall also have an identifying
insignia on the roof. (Ord. 706, 10-20-1997)
5-8-7: RECEIPT AND DISCHARGE OF PASSENGERS:
Drivers of vehicles licensed hereunder shall not receive or discharge
passengers in the roadway, but shall pull up to the right-hand sidewalk as
nearly as possible, or in the absence of a sidewalk, to the extreme right-hand
side of the road and there receive or discharge passengers. (Ord. 706, 10-20-
1997)
5-8-8: SEATING CAPACITY:
No driver of a vehicle licensed hereunder shall permit more persons to be
carried in said vehicle than the number of available seat belts in the vehicle.
(Ord. 706, 10-20-1997)
5-8-9: STATE OPERATOR'S LICENSE REQUIRED:
No person shall operate a vehicle licensed hereunder upon the streets of the
City, and no person who owns or controls a vehicle licensed hereunder shall
permit it to be operated upon the streets of the City unless the driver for
such vehicle shall have first obtained a State of Idaho operator's license for
the operation of taxicabs or vehicles for hire. (Ord. 706, 10-20-1997)
5-8-10: DISPLAY OF OPERATOR'S LICENSE:
Every driver of a vehicle licensed under the provisions of this chapter shall
display the appropriate State of Idaho operator's license for taxicabs and
vehicles for hire at all times when driving such vehicle and shall affix the
license in a conspicuous place where it shall be in full view of the passengers
of the vehicle. (Ord. 706, 10-20-1997)
CHAPTER 9
TRAILER COURTS AND TRAILER COACHES
SECTION:
5-9-1: Definitions
5-9-2: Application; Trailer Court
5-9-3: Trailer Court License
5-9-4: Register
5-9-5: Domestic Animals
5-9-6: License Transfer
5-9-7: Application; Trailer Coach
5-9-8: Trailer Coach License Fee
5-9-9: Location Of Trailer Coaches
5-9-10: Permit Renewal; Trailer Coach
5-9-11: Location Restrictions
5-9-12: Revocation
5-9-13: Posting Of License
5-9-1: DEFINITIONS:
DEPENDENT TRAILER COACH: One which does not have a water closet and bathtub or
shower.
INDEPENDENT TRAILER COACH: One that has a water closet and a bathtub or shower.
SERVICE BUILDING: A building housing communal toilet, laundry and other
sanitary facilities necessary for the health and convenience of the trailer
occupants.
TRAILER COACH: A vehicle without means of self-propulsion, but licensable as a
conveyance on public streets or highways, and which is constructed to permit
occupancy as a dwelling or sleeping place for one or more persons.
TRAILER COACH SPACE: A plot of ground within a trailer court designated for the
accommodation of one trailer coach.
TRAILER COURT: Any plot of ground upon which two (2) or more occupied trailer
coaches are located. (1959 Code)
5-9-2: APPLICATION; TRAILER COURT:
Applications for a trailer court license shall be filed with and issued by the
City Clerk. Application shall be in writing signed by the applicant and shall
contain the following:
   A.   The name and address of the applicant.
   B.   The location and legal description of the trailer court.
   C.   Such further information as may be requested by the Governing Body to
enable it to determine if the proposed location will comply with legal
requirements, including a sketch or plot plan designating numbered trailer
spaces.
No change or alteration in the plot plan shall be made without first making a
written application for such change or alteration to the Governing Body and
receiving a written permit therefrom.
The Governing Body shall investigate the location and if it is found to be in
compliance with all provisions of this chapter and all other applicable
chapters or statutes, application may be approved. (1959 Code)
5-9-3: TRAILER COURT LICENSE:
Any person who maintains or operates a trailer court must first obtain a
license from the City Clerk which license must be approved by the Governing
Body of the City. The fee for such trailer court shall be as established in the
master fee schedule. (1959 Code; amd. Ord. 925, 10-1-2018)
5-9-4: REGISTER:
It shall be the duty of the licensee to keep a register containing a record of
all trailer coaches occupying space within the court. The register shall
contain the following information:
   A.   Name and address of each occupant in each trailer coach.
   B.   Make, model and year of all automobiles and trailer coaches.
   C.   License numbers and owner of each trailer coach and automobile by which
it is towed.
   D.   The state issuing such licenses.
   E.   The date of arrival and departure of each trailer coach and the number
or other identification of the space or spaces occupied. The court shall keep
the register available for inspection at all times by law enforcement officers,
public health officials and other officials whose duties necessitate
acquisition of the information contained in the register. The register records
shall not be destroyed until after a period of three (3) years following the
date of registration. (1959 Code)
5-9-5: DOMESTIC ANIMALS:
No domestic animals or house pets shall be allowed to run at large or commit
any nuisances within the limits of a trailer court. (1959 Code)
5-9-6: LICENSE TRANSFER:
All licenses issued hereunder for a trailer court and trailer coach shall be
personal to the licensee and be nontransferable without the written consent of
the governing body first being obtained. (1959 Code)
5-9-7: APPLICATION; TRAILER COACH:
Application for a trailer coach license shall be filed with and issued by the
City Clerk. Application shall be in writing signed by the applicant and shall
contain the following:
   A.   The name and address of the applicant.
   B.   The location and description where trailer coach is to be parked.
   C.   Such further information as may be requested by the governing body.
(1959 Code)
5-9-8: TRAILER COACH LICENSE FEE:
There shall be imposed by the City retroactive to the date of January 1, 1965,
no trailer coach fee charged to each applicant for licenses required hereunder.
However, a license and application therefor must be made in accordance with the
terms of this Chapter. All licenses so issued shall expire on December 31 of
each year. (Ord. 372, 1-11-1965)
5-9-9: LOCATION OF TRAILER COACHES:
The use of trailer coaches as trailer or otherwise, occupied by one or more
persons, except in an approved public or private trailer court, shall be
considered as a public nuisance unless the yards surrounding it comply with the
requirements for a dwelling as established by the zoning provisions of this
Code 1 . (Ord. 328, 8-10-1959)
 
Notes
1 1. See Title 10 of this Code.
5-9-10: PERMIT RENEWAL; TRAILER COACH:
It shall be unlawful for any person to occupy a trailer coach or for any person
who is the owner, renter or lessee of any property within the City to erect or
give consent for the placement and occupancy of any trailer house within the
City except in an approved public trailer court or in an approved trailer coach
space.
It shall be unlawful to park a trailer coach, whether occupied or not, on any
public thoroughfare or public place, other than in an approved trailer court
for more than four (4) hours.
Trailer coaches may be parked on private property and occupied by a person or
persons for a period of time specified in the permit issued under Section
5-9-8 of this Chapter. A permit for such use and occupancy must be obtained in
compliance with Section
5-9-8, within forty eight (48) hours after the trailer is parked. (Ord. 328, 8-
10-1959)
5-9-11: LOCATION RESTRICTIONS:
Placement and use of trailer coaches occupied by any person on other than
approved public or private courts must be so arranged as not to interfere with
the rights and privileges of adjacent property owners, each occupied trailer
coach being considered as a separate dwelling house under the laws of the
zoning ordinance 1 . (1959 Code)
 
Notes
1 1. See Title 10 of this Code.
5-9-12: REVOCATION:
The governing body may revoke or suspend any license issued in this Chapter
when such licensee shall have been found guilty of a violation of this Chapter
or any part of this Code. (1959 Code)
5-9-13: POSTING OF LICENSE:
A license issued under this Chapter shall be conspicuously posted on the
individual trailer coach not located within a trailer court or in the office of
or on the premises of the trailer court. (1959 Code)
CHAPTER 10
HOTELS AND MOTELS
SECTION:
5-10-1: Hotel Regulations
5-10-2: Motel Regulations
5-10-1: HOTEL REGULATIONS:
   A.   Definition: Every building maintained or advertised as a public lodging
house or where more than six (6) rooms are provided for sleeping accommodations
shall be known as a hotel.
   B.   Fire Protection Equipment: The Fire Chief, or other officer designated
by the governing body, shall survey each hotel and specify suitable fire
detecting devices or extinguishing appliances which shall be provided.
Such devices or appliances may consist of automatic sprinkler or water spray
systems, standpipe and hose, fixed or portable fire extinguishers or other
suitable fire extinguishing systems.
   C.   Maintenance Of Equipment: Fire protective or extinguishing systems or
appliances which have been installed in compliance with any permit or order, or
according to any provisions of this Code, shall be maintained in operative
condition at all times and it shall be unlawful for any owner or occupant to
reduce the effectiveness of the protection so required.
   D.   Inspection: It shall be the duty of the Fire Chief and the Health
Officer, or other officers so designated by the governing body, to make
periodic and regular inspections of every hotel and to make regular reports to
the governing body of such hotel or hotels concerning regulations imposed by
this Code.
   E.   Hotel Register: A register shall be maintained at every hotel and each
guest shall be required to register his name and home address. The date of
arrival and departure shall be clearly indicated and the register shall be
maintained for a period of at least one year following registration. The
register shall be open for inspection to any authorized person. (1959 Code)
5-10-2: MOTEL REGULATIONS:
   A.   Building Permit Required: Before construction of a motel is started, an
application for a permit for such construction shall be submitted to the City
Clerk. The City Clerk shall present such application to the governing body for
its approval. Only after approval of the governing body shall a permit for
construction of a motel be issued.
   B.   Service Station Restrictions: Automobile service stations shall be
located no closer than fifty feet (50') to any motel.
   C.   Parking Space On Premises: Each unit of a motel or tourist court shall
be provided with an assigned parking space entirely on the premises.
   D.   Minimum Requirements: The minimum space for each unit shall be twelve
feet by twenty feet (12' x 20') and shall contain one full bath, toilet
facilities, dressing compartment and sleeping room.
   E.   Existing Standards: The plumbing, heating and ventilation components
shall meet all local fire, plumbing and building code requirements.
   F.   Application To Include Plan: Each application for a motel or tourist
court shall be submitted with a complete plan, including the plot plan and
adjacent buildings, parking arrangement and driveways, unit sizes, plumbing and
heating layout, accessory uses, materials to be used, front and rear elevations
and architectural design.
   G.   Guests Required To Register: Every operator of a motel shall maintain a
register in which each guest shall register his name, home address and license
number of the vehicle in which he is traveling. The date of his arrival and
departure shall also be recorded. Such register shall be available to any
authorized person inspecting the motel and shall be preserved for a period of
not less than one year. (1959 Code)
TITLE 6
POLICE REGULATIONS
CHAPTER 1
GENERAL OFFENSES
SECTION:
6-1-1: Effect Of Regulations
6-1-2: Barbed Wire And Electric Fences
6-1-3: Cruelty To Animals
6-1-4: Deposit Of Injurious Material On Thoroughfares
6-1-5: Disorderly Conduct
6-1-6: Expectorating (Spitting) On Sidewalks Or In Public Buildings
6-1-7: Offense, General
6-1-8: Indecent Exposure
6-1-9: Keeping Of Junk Restricted
6-1-10: Loudspeakers Or Sound Trucks
6-1-11: Lug Wheels Prohibited
6-1-12: Mufflers; Unnecessary Noise
6-1-13: Obscene Conduct
6-1-14: Water Flowing Upon Streets
6-1-15: Windowsills To Be Kept Clear
6-1-16: Abandoned Iceboxes, Refrigerators Or Containers
6-1-17:    Weapons Prohibited
6-1-18:    Trapping Regulations
6-1-1: EFFECT OF REGULATIONS:
   A.   It shall be unlawful for any person to do any act forbidden or fail to
perform any act required herein. (Ord. 753, 10-21-2002)
   B.   Any violation of this chapter shall constitute a misdemeanor and be
punishable by imprisonment in the County Jail not exceeding six (6) months, or
by a fine as established in the master fee schedule, or by both. (Ord. 753, 10-
21-2002; amd. Ord. 925, 10-1-2018)
6-1-2: BARBED WIRE AND ELECTRIC FENCES:
It shall be unlawful for any person to erect or maintain any electric fence or
other fence constructed in whole or in part of barbed wire or to use barbed
wire as a guard to any parking lot or parcel of land.
   A.   Barbed Wire Fences:
      1.   Barbed wire fences shall be allowed within the incorporated limits
of the City in the following places only:
         a.   In any zone which permits the maintenance of livestock.
         b.   As a guard atop a fence of at least six feet (6') high for
security purposes within the industrial or commercial zone of the City.
   B.   Electric Fences: Electric fences shall not be permitted at any place
within the incorporated limits of the City. (Ord. 753, 10-21-2002)
6-1-3: CRUELTY TO ANIMALS:
It shall be unlawful for any person to torture or beat cruelly, starve or
otherwise ill treat any animal in his care or charge, whether belonging to
themselves or any other person. (Ord. 753, 10-21-2002)
6-1-4: DEPOSITS OF INJURIOUS MATERIAL ON THOROUGHFARES:
It shall be unlawful for any person to deposit, place or allow to remain in or
upon any public thoroughfare any material or substance injurious to person or
property. (Ord. 753, 10-21-2002)
6-1-5: DISORDERLY CONDUCT:
Every person is guilty of disorderly conduct when that person willfully engages
in violent, tumultuous or offensive conduct; or by threatening, quarrelling, or
challenging to fight another person; or fights with another person in a public
place; or makes noise that is unreasonable, considering the nature of the
actor’s conduct, location, time of day or night, and other factors that would
govern the conduct of a reasonably prudent person under the circumstances; or
engages in violent, noisy or riotous behavior that would be frightening or
offensive to a reasonable person who might be expected to be in the vicinity.
(Ord. 753, 10-21-2002; amd. Ord. 955, 3-21-2022)
6-1-6: EXPECTORATING (SPITTING) ON SIDEWALKS OR IN PUBLIC BUILDINGS:
It shall be unlawful for any person to expectorate or spit upon any sidewalk,
public way or upon the floor of any public building or room used for public
assemblies. (Ord. 753, 10-21-2002)
6-1-7: OFFENSE, GENERAL:
It shall be unlawful for any person to commit any act or fail to perform any
requirement which is prohibited or required by state law or city code, insofar
as such laws are applicable to municipal government. (Ord. 753, 10-21-2002)
6-1-8: INDECENT EXPOSURE:
It shall be unlawful for any person to appear in a state of nudity or in any
indecent or lewd dress or condition in any public place or in any such place to
make any indecent exposure of his/her person or private parts thereof or the
private parts of another or to conduct themselves in a lewd or lascivious
manner. (Ord. 753, 10-21-2002)
6-1-9: KEEPING OF JUNK RESTRICTED:
It shall be unlawful for any person to store or keep any old articles or
materials which may be classified as junk, adjacent to or in close proximity to
any school, house, church, public park, public grounds, business buildings, or
residences without first providing proper and tight buildings for the storage
of same. (Ord. 753, 10-21-2002)
6-1-10: LOUDSPEAKERS OR SOUND TRUCKS:
It shall be unlawful to play, operate or use any device known as a sound truck,
loudspeaker or sound amplifier, radio or phonograph, with loudspeaker or sound
amplifier or any instrument of any kind or character which emits loud and
raucous noise and is attached to and upon any vehicle unless such person in
charge of such vehicle shall have first applied to and received a permit from
the city of Grangeville to operate any such vehicle so equipped. (Ord. 753, 10-
21-2002)
6-1-11: LUG WHEELS PROHIBITED:
It shall be unlawful for tractors, or other vehicles with wheels injurious to
pavement to be permitted upon the public thoroughfares unless the operator of
such vehicle shall first plank such streets or place rubber treads on wheels.
(Ord. 753, 10-21-2002)
6-1-12: MUFFLERS; UNNECESSARY NOISE:
It shall be unlawful for any person to operate a motor vehicle which shall, at
all times, be equipped with a muffler upon the exhaust thereof in good working
order and in constant operation to prevent excessive or unusual noise and it
shall be unlawful for any person operating any motor vehicle to use a cutout,
bypass or similar muffler elimination appliance. (Ord. 753, 10-21-2002)
6-1-13: OBSCENE CONDUCT:
It shall be unlawful for any person to urinate or stool in any place open to
the public view, or to be guilty of any lewd, lascivious or obscene conduct or
to sing any lewd or obscene song, ballad or other words in any public place or
any other place where other persons are present or to indecently, exhibit any
animal. (Ord. 753, 10-21-2002)
6-1-14: WATER FLOWING UPON STREETS:
It shall be unlawful for any person to allow any water to flow into or upon any
public thoroughfare. (Ord. 753, 10-21-2002)
6-1-15: WINDOWSILLS TO BE KEPT CLEAR:
It shall be unlawful for any person to place or keep on any windowsill, porch
or other projection above the first story of any building abutting on any
sidewalk any article which might do injury by falling upon any person on the
sidewalk in front of such building, unless said article be securely fastened or
protected by screens. (Ord. 753, 10-21-2002)
6-1-16: ABANDONED ICEBOXES, REFRIGERATORS OR CONTAINERS:
It shall be unlawful for any person to leave or permit to remain outside of any
dwelling, building or other structure, or within any unoccupied or abandoned
building, dwelling or other structure under their control, in a place
accessible to children, any abandoned, unattended or discarded icebox,
refrigerator or other container which has a door or lid, snaplock, or other
locking device which may not be released from the inside, without first
removing said door or lid, snaplock or other locking device, or by first
fastening, bolting or locking the same in such a manner that it is impossible
to open the same by the use of the hands. (Ord. 753, 10-21-2002)
6-1-17: WEAPONS PROHIBITED:
   A.   Definition: Whenever the term “weapon” is used in this section, the
term shall mean any instrument, used in the propulsion of shot, shell or
bullets or other harmful objects by the action of gunpowder exploded within it,
or by the action of compressed air within it, or by the power of springs,
rubber bands, or by the power of a bow and string, and including what are
commonly known as air rifles and BB guns, slingshots, bow and arrows, etc.
   B.   Concealed Weapons: Without a properly issued concealed weapons permit,
it shall be unlawful for any person to carry concealed upon his person any
brass knuckles, revolver, pistol, dagger, stilettos or other deadly weapon.
   C.   Discharge Of Weapons Prohibited: It shall be unlawful for any person to
discharge weapons of any kind or description within the limits of the city;
provided however, that this shall not apply to police officers in the discharge
of their duties.
   D.   Exceptions; Permits: The city council may at any time, upon receipt of
proper application, grant permits to shooting galleries, gun clubs and others
for shooting in fixed localities and under specified rules. Such permits shall
be in writing attested by the city clerk conforming to such requirements as the
city council shall demand, and the permit thus issued shall be subject to
revocation at any time by action of the governing body. (Ord. 753, 10-21-2002)
6-1-18: TRAPPING REGULATIONS:
   A.   Definitions:
   TRAP: Any mechanical device or snare which is designed to hold, capture,
and/or kill an animal including, but not limited to, live traps, steel jaw
foothold traps, padded jaw traps, body gripping (Conibear) traps, snares,
deadfalls, leg hold type traps, or similar devices.
   B.   Setting Traps Prohibited; Exceptions: Unless authorized by the Idaho
department of fish and game, pursuant to Idaho Code title 36, chapter 11, no
person shall set a trap to catch an animal (other than a mouse, rat, gopher,
vole, or mole) within the city limits, except a person specifically authorized
by the council or by the chief of police or designee.
   C.   Penalties: Any person violating these provisions shall be deemed guilty
of an infraction and, upon conviction thereof, shall be punished pursuant to
this code and the Idaho Code, unless otherwise specifically provided for. (Ord.
881, 12-17-2012)
CHAPTER 2
ANIMAL CONTROL
SECTION:
6-2-1: Purpose
6-2-2: Definitions
6-2-3: Violations
6-2-4: Fees For Licensing, Impounding And Boarding
6-2-5: Procedures
6-2-6: Duties Of Animal Control Officer
6-2-7: Impoundment Of Dogs And Other Animals
6-2-8: Violations And Remedies Cumulative
6-2-9: Penalty For Violation
6-2-1: PURPOSE:
The city is concerned about the welfare of dogs and other animals, owned,
harbored and possessed within the city limits and about the responsibility of
the owners, harborers and other persons possessing such animals. This chapter
provides for the licensing of dogs and for the disposition of dogs found
without such license having been paid; prohibiting imitation license tags;
providing for the examination for rabies and the disposition of rabid dogs;
providing for impounding of dogs, and fees therefor; providing for the
prohibition of any dog or other animals, running at large; providing a penalty,
for keeping or harboring any dog without paying a license therefor or
permitting any dog to run at large; prohibit the harboring of a barking dog;
prohibiting dogs and other animals in city parks; prohibiting the running at
large of female dogs in heat; prohibiting a vicious dog to run at large;
prohibiting a sick dog to run at large; prohibiting the owning of, harboring of
or possession of exotic animals; providing a penalty thereof; providing for the
duties of the chief of police and his designated assistant; declaring
interference with any officer to be unlawful. (Ord. 699, 2-18-1997; amd. Ord.
939, 11-18-2019)
6-2-2: DEFINITIONS:
                   Any domestic animal that has been tamed and kept by humans as a work animal,
ANIMAL:            food source, or pet. Domestic cats are excluded from this chapter, unless
                   specifically included herein.
ANIMAL CONTROL     The chief of police; all police officers of the city; and any other person
OFFICER:           designated by the city as animal control officer.
                   Whenever any dog or other animal shall be found upon any of the streets or
AT LARGE; DOGS/    alleys of the city, or on the premises of any persons, firm or corporation who
ANIMALS:           are not the owner of said animal, and not being actually led or driven by some
                   person in charge, they shall be deemed at large.
                   A small carnivorous mammal long domesticated and kept by man as a pet for
CAT:               catching rats and mice. This does not include any other members of the cat
                   family.
DANGEROUS DOG:     Any dog declared dangerous as provided in this chapter.
DOG:               Any member, male or female, of the family of Canis familiaris.
EXOTIC ANIMAL/WILD Any animal which is considered a wild animal or is inherently dangerous.
ANIMALS:
                   To own or keep a dog within the city limits. It shall be prima facie evidence
                   that a person is harboring a dog if the person is listed as the owner of the dog
HARBOR/HARBORIN G: on any application for dog licensing; or is over eighteen (18) years of age and
                   resides at or is in physical control of a premises, or part thereof, on which a
                   dog remains or to which it customarily returns daily for food or water.
HARBORER/OWNER:    Any person harboring or keeping a dog within the corporate limits of the city.
                   Any premises, other than a veterinary office, on which four (4) or more dogs are
KENNEL:            maintained, harbored, possessed, boarded, bred or cared for, trained, or sold,
                   which are over four (4) months of age.
LEASH:             A leash, lead, cord, or chain not more than ten feet (10') in length, by which
                   an animal is physically controlled by the person accompanying it.
NEUTERED/SPAYED    Any dog rendered incapable of producing offspring by surgery or other veterinary
DOG:               medical procedure.
                   All real property under a harborer's ownership, lease or control inside the
PREMISES:          inner line of a sidewalk, or if no sidewalk, inside the curb, ditch or shoulder
                   marking the edge of the traveled or used portion of the public right of way.
                   Premises also includes the inside of a closed motor vehicle.
                   A vaccination given by a licensed veterinarian, to a dog for the prevention of
RABIES             rabies, and a certificate of vaccination is issued, with a certification that
VACCINATION:    the vaccination is valid for a specified period of time as designated by the
                   veterinarian.
                   A dog is under control if:
                   A.   The dog is confined within the boundaries of the harborer's premises; or
                   B.   The dog is not on the harborer's premises but is confined within a vehicle
UNDER CONTROL:     or in the control of a responsible person by use of a leash not exceeding ten
                   feet (10') in length; or
                   C.   The dog is secure in the bed of a vehicle in such a manner that, the animal
                   cannot reach the side rails of the vehicle bed.
                   (Ord. 699, 2-18-1997; amd. Ord. 745, 1-7-2002; Ord. 939, 11-18-2019)
 
6-2-3: VIOLATIONS:
   A.   Dogs/Animals Running At Large Prohibited: All owners/harborers
responsible for dogs/animals kept within the city limits shall keep such
animals under control or confined at all times. It shall be unlawful to allow
dogs/animals to run at large. Violations of this subsection shall be an
infraction and shall be punishable as provided in Idaho Code section 18-113(A).
   B.   Poultry Running At Large Prohibited: It shall be unlawful to allow fowl
or poultry to run at large. Violation shall be a misdemeanor.
   C.   Keeping Of Stallions, Jacks, Bulls and Hogs: It shall be unlawful to
keep a stallion, jack, bull or hog within the city limits. Violation shall be a
misdemeanor.
   D.   Permitting Horses On Sidewalks: It shall be unlawful for any person to
allow or permit any horse, owned by him or in his custody or control, to go
upon, be ridden upon or be led upon any sidewalk in the city. Violation shall
be a misdemeanor.
   E.   Shod Horses On Paved Streets: It shall be unlawful for any person to
permit any shod horse, owned by or in their control, to go upon, be ridden upon
or be led upon any paved street in the city, when such street has been closed
to such traffic, and posted, by order of the chief of police or street
superintendent when it appears that such traffic would damage the surface of
said streets. Violation shall be a misdemeanor.
   F.   License Required: It shall be unlawful for any owner/harborer to own,
keep or possess a dog within the city without procuring a license as provided
by this chapter. Violation shall be a misdemeanor. Any person visiting the city
for not longer than thirty (30) days, and having a dog licensed from another
city shall be exempt.
   G.   Collar And Tag: Every dog shall at all times wear a substantial durable
collar to which shall be securely attached the required license. Violation
shall be a misdemeanor.
   H.   Imitation License Tags Prohibited. It shall be unlawful for any owner/
harborer to allow any dog kept or possessed within the city to wear any license
tag or indicia of licensing other than a valid license tag issued under this
chapter for the dog wearing this tag. Violation shall be a misdemeanor. This
section shall not prohibit the wearing of nonlicense tags for the purpose of
identification or rabies.
   I.   Female Dogs in Heat: It shall be unlawful for any owner/harborer to
allow any female dog in heat, outside of a controlled area when in heat.
Violation shall be a misdemeanor. Any dog at large, in heat, may be disposed of
by the animal control officer without giving any notice.
   J.   Vicious Dogs Within The City Prohibited: It shall be unlawful for any
owner/harborer to maintain a vicious dog within the city limits. Violation
shall be a misdemeanor.
   K.   Vicious Or Sick Dog At Large Prohibited: It shall be unlawful for any
owner/harborer to allow a vicious or sick dog to run at large. Violation shall
be a misdemeanor.
   L.      Dogs and Other Animals Prohibited in City Parks: With the exception
from the creek to the east end of Grangeville Lions Club Park as designated, it
shall be unlawful for any owner/harborer to allow any dog or other animal to be
within or upon those areas known as city parks: i.e., Pioneer park, Grangeville
Lions Club park, Jaycee park. Violation shall be a misdemeanor.
         It shall be unlawful for any owner/harborer to allow any dog, or other
animal to deposit feces within or upon City parks. Violation shall be an
infraction, punishable by a fine as established in the master fee schedule.
   M.   Barking Dogs: No person shall own, harbor or otherwise be responsible
for any dog within the City that shall bark or growl, so as to unreasonably
disturb the peace or quiet of any other person. Violation shall be a
misdemeanor.
   N.   Exotic Animals: It shall be unlawful for any owner/harborer to own,
possess, or harbor any exotic animal within the City limits without application
to and approval by the City Council. Violation shall be a misdemeanor.
   O.   Kennels: It shall be unlawful for any owner/harborer to maintain a
kennel within the City limits, with the exception of those kennels that are
allowed in accordance with the zoning title. 1   Violation shall be a
misdemeanor.
   P.   Nonvaccinated Dog: It shall be unlawful for any owner/harborer to own,
possess, or harbor a dog within the city limits that does not have a valid
rabies vaccination. Violation shall be a misdemeanor.
   Q.   Interference Prohibited: It shall be unlawful for any person to
knowingly hinder, molest or interfere with any animal control officer in the
discharge of any of their duties. In addition, it shall be unlawful for any
person to attempt to remove and/or remove any dog or dogs from the city pound
or the possession of the animal control officer, without the consent of the
animal control officer or otherwise as provided by this chapter. Violation
shall be a misdemeanor.
   R.   General Offense: It shall be unlawful for any owner/harborer to:
      1.   Allow any dog or animal under their control to scatter garbage,
refuse or debris.
      2.   Allow any dog or animal under their control to chase any person,
vehicle or other animal.
      3.   Allow any dog or animal under their control to deposit fecal
material on any property not that of its owner/harborer without immediately
removing same from the property.
      4.   Harbor one or more dogs, cats, or animals in such a manner that the
keeping of the dogs, cats, or animals results in a nauseous, foul or offensive
odor or so as to create a public nuisance.
      5.   Harbor a dog, cat, or animal and fail to provide the dog, cat, or
animal with food, water, shelter, or necessary veterinary care. Violation shall
be a misdemeanor. (Ord. 699, 2-18-1997; amd. Ord. 746, 1-7-2002, Ord. 896, 3-2-
2015; Ord. 925, 10-1-2018; Ord. 939, 11-18-2019)
 
Notes
1    1. See title 10 of this Code.
6-2-4: FEES FOR LICENSING, IMPOUNDING AND BOARDING:
All fees shall be as established in the master fee schedule.
All owners/harborers, prior to having license issued, must display to the
licensing authority a current rabies vaccination.
To receive the spayed or neutered rate, a valid certification from a licensed
veterinarian, showing the dog has been neutered or spayed, must be displayed to
the licensing authority. (Res. 136, 2-18-1997; amd. Ord. 925, 10-1-2018; Ord.
939, 11-18-2019)
6-2-5: PROCEDURES:
   A.   Violations: All owners/harboreres shall receive from the animal control
officer one written warning for violations of subsections
6-2-3A through P of this chapter with the exceptions of subsections
6-2-3I, J, K and P of this chapter. All owners/harborers that have received a
written warning and not corrected the violation shall be issued a uniform
citation.
      The animal control officer, shall be authorized to issue a citation to
any person whom the officer has probable cause to believe has violated any of
the provision of this Chapter. The citation shall be issued upon a form that is
approved for use for the prosecution of general misdemeanors by the
Magistrate's Division of the District Court for the Second Judicial District,
for the State of Idaho, at Grangeville. The citation shall be prepared in
accordance with the existing statutes of the State of Idaho for processing
general misdemeanors as from time to time shall be prescribed by the Idaho
State Legislature.
      1.   A violation of subsection
6-2-3I, Female Dogs In Heat, will immediately be impounded, any animal in heat
may be disposed of by the animal control officer without giving any notice.
      2.   A violation of subsection
6-2-3K, Vicious Or Sick Dog At Large, the animal control officer, may
immediately and without giving notice, dispose of by destroying in a humane
manner any dog found running at large which in the judgment of the officer:
         a.   Displays symptoms of contagious disease; or
         b.   Displays serious physical injury or illness such that the officer
deems, in the officer's sole discretion, that it is necessary to destroy the
animal to prevent further suffering; or
         c.   Displays vicious or aggressive behavior which poses an imminent
risk of physical injury to any person and the dog cannot, in the discretion of
the animal control officer, be taken into control for impoundment by reasonable
humane methods.
      3.   A violation of subsection
6-2-3J, Vicious Dogs Within The City, the animal control officer, may declare a
dog to be a dangerous dog if, upon investigation of any complaint, incident or
information otherwise provided, the officer finds that:
         a.   The dog has, whether or not under control, aggressively bitten
any person, domestic animal or fowl or maliciously damaged or destroyed
personal property of another:
         b.   The dog has been declared dangerous, vicious or other similar
declaration by any governmental authority.
      If the officer makes said declaration, the officer shall notify the
owner/harborer of the declaration and the manner and time limits in which an
appeal of the declaration may be taken. In addition, a uniform citation shall
be issued to the owner/harborer for violation of subsection
6-2-3J. Said notice shall be in writing and served by, personal service, or
regular first class U.S. mail addressed to the last known mailing address of
the owner/harborer, with service being effective on the date of mailing.
      4.   The officer may impound the dog declared to be dangerous, including
but not limited to impounding of the dog during the pendency of any appeal
proceeding. The owner/harborer of the dog shall be liable for all costs and
fees of impoundment regardless of the final disposition of the case.
      The owner/harborer of a dog declared dangerous shall have five (5)
business days from the date of service of the written declaration to request a
hearing appealing the declaration. The request shall be in writing, identifying
the name, address and telephone number of the requesting party, and shall be
served upon the City Clerk within the time and in the manner above provided. In
the event no hearing is requested within the time and in the manner above
provided the officer may dispose of the dog in a humane manner, without further
notice to the owner/harborer.
      If a hearing is requested, a hearing shall be held within fifteen (15)
days of the date, the request for hearing is received by the City Clerk, or at
such other times as set by the City Council and the requesting party.
         a.   The City Council shall constitute the hearing panel and shall
hear the appeal. The hearing shall be informal and the Idaho Rules of Evidence
shall not apply. The owner/harborer and the animal control officer, or other
representative of the City shall be given the opportunity to submit evidence,
present witnesses and be heard on the matter, including the right of cross-
examination.
         b.   In determining whether the dog is dangerous, the hearing panel
may consider among other evidence, past incidents, provocation for the
dangerous behavior, whether the conduct occurred on the premises where the dog
was harbored, the legal status of the alleged victim on the premises and any
other fact or allegation relating to the incident from which the declaration
arises.
      If the hearing panel shall find that the declaration was proper, the
hearing panel shall either:
         a.   Direct the animal control officer to dispose of the dog as
directed by this Chapter.
         b.   Direct that the dog may be released to the owner/harborer on such
conditions as the hearing panel shall deem in the best interest of the City,
which may include, but are not limited to, that:
            (1)   The dog will be removed from the City limits immediately
following release and not allowed to return.
            (2)   Require the owner/harborer to take steps sufficient to
confine the dog in a manner to prevent harm to the public.
            (3)   Require the owner/harborer to provide a surety bond or proof
of liability insurance for compensation of those who may suffer injury by
reason of harboring of a dangerous dog.
      The decision of the hearing panel shall become final, unless the decision
is appealed to the District Court within three (3) days, following the date of
the decision.
      5.   A violation of subsection
6-2-3P, Non-Vaccinated Dog shall result in the immediate issuance of a uniform
citation to the owner/harborer of the animal, with written instructions to have
the dog vaccinated within three (3) days.
   B.   Licenses; Application And Fees: All dog licenses shall be issued for
the calendar year January 1 through December 31 of each and every year. The
owner/harborer shall make application to the animal control officer, or the
City clerk's office, and pay a license fee as established in the master fee
schedule, for each dog maintained within the City limits.
      1.   Upon receipt of the application and payment of the fees, and upon
issuance of a receipt, stating the owner's/harborer's name, sex of the dog,
breed, color, age, address, phone number, any markings of the animal, and
whether the animal is neutered/spayed, a metal license shall be issued bearing
the number corresponding to that upon the receipt.
      2.   Upon satisfactory proof that a license has been lost, a new tag of a
